Order Between Witr and Fajr: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on order between witr and fajr prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of Fajr when witr was missed and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the obligation of order (tartib).

Core Idea
If witr is wajib, order with fard is compulsory; if sunnah, it is not — the ruling hinges on witr's legal status.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a person remembers after praying Fajr that he did not perform witr. Is his Fajr valid? The answer depends on whether witr is wajib or sunnah, and whether order between prayers of different categories is required. We explore the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and we see how a difference in usul leads to a difference in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The base text states that it is not valid (la yajuz) to pray Fajr if one remembers leaving witr. This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Understand the basis: order (tartib)
The commentary explains that this ruling is a branch of the principle that order between prayers is obligatory (fard). Validity is lost if order is omitted.
The principle of tartib is well-established among the five daily fard prayers.
3
Locate the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on whether witr is wajib or sunnah. This status determines whether order applies.
Abu Hanifa: witr is wajib. Sahibayn: witr is sunnah.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: For Abu Hanifa, Fajr is invalid and must be repeated after witr. For the Sahibayn, Fajr is valid and only the missed witr needs to be performed.
The dispute directly affects the worshiper's obligation to repeat Fajr.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, due to precaution and the established practice of early Hanafi masters.
This is the position used for fatwa in most Hanafi contexts.

Source Text

(فلم يجز فجر مَن ذَكَرَ أنه لم يوتر) ، هذا تفريع لقوله : والوتر، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له خلافاً لهما بناء على وجوب الوتر عنده. [١) قوله : فلم يجز ؛ تفريع على كون الترتيب فرضاً، بحيث يفوت الجواز بفوته ؛ أي لو صلى صلاة الفجر ذاكراً أنه لم يؤد الوتر لم يَجُزْ فَجْرَه ، فيقضي الوتر أولاً ثمَّ يُصلي الفجر عند أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنّ الـوتـر عـنده واجب ، وهو في حكـم الفـرض عملاً، فيكون الترتيب بينه وبين غيره من الفرائض فرضاً، كالترتيب بين الفرائض الخمسة. (٢) قوله : خلافاً لهما ؛ فإنّ الوتر عندهما سُنّة من السنن، ولا يفرض الترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن اتفاقاً. [٣]قوله : بناء ؛ أي بنى هذا التفريع بناء على وجوب...الخ، أو هو متعلق بقوله هذا عند أبي حنيفة .
It is not valid the Fajr of one who remembered that he did not pray witr. This is a branch of his statement: 'and witr'. This according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions, based on the obligation of witr according to him. [1) His statement: 'It is not valid'; a branching on the condition that order is obligatory, such that validity is lost by its omission; i.e., if one prayed the Fajr prayer while remembering that he had not performed witr, his Fajr is not valid. So he should pray witr first then pray Fajr according to Abu Hanifa, because witr according to him is obligatory (wajib), and it is in the ruling of a fard in practice, so order between it and other obligations is obligatory, like order between the five prayers. (2) His statement: 'contrary to them two'; because witr according to them is a sunnah from the sunnahs, and order between obligations and sunnahs is not obligatory by consensus. [3] His statement: 'based'; i.e., he built this branching based on obligation...etc., or it is connected to his statement 'this according to Abu Hanifa'.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that if someone remembers that he did not pray witr after he has already prayed Fajr, his Fajr prayer is not valid. The commentary explains that this is a branch of the earlier rule that order (tartib) between prayers is obligatory. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. According to Abu Hanifa, witr is wajib, and wajib in the Hanafi school is a binding obligation, though slightly lower than fard. In terms of order, witr is treated like a fard. Therefore, just as order is required between the five daily fard prayers, order is required between a fard and witr. Hence, one must pray the missed witr before the Fajr prayer. According to the two companions, witr is sunnah, not wajib, and order is not required between sunnah and fard. Therefore, the Fajr prayer would be valid even if witr was missed, though it is blameworthy to leave witr. The commentary clarifies that Abu Hanifa's position is based on the actual obligation (wujub) of witr in his view. The footnote also explains the terminology: 'branching' refers to the fact that this ruling follows from the principle that order is obligatory. The phrase 'contrary to them two' indicates the disagreement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This is a classic example of how differences in the categorization of an act (wajib vs sunnah) lead to different practical rulings regarding order and validity.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order in which prayers should be performed; if one misses a prayer, it must be made up before the next prayer.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib by Abu Hanifa and sunnah by the Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on the Fajr prayer of a person who remembers that he did not perform witr?
A) His Fajr is valid and he does not need to repeat it.
B) His Fajr is not valid; he must pray witr first and then repeat Fajr.
C) His Fajr is valid but he must repeat witr after Fajr.
D) His Fajr is not valid, but he only needs to repeat witr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that witr is wajib, thus order with Fajr is required; if witr is missed, Fajr must be repeated after making up witr.

Repeating Isha and Sunnah When Fard is Invalid: The Follower Principle
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repeating witr when Isha is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the sunnah is a follower of the fard, and distinguish when witr is independent, in cases where the fard prayer was invalid.

Core Idea
The sunnah follows the fard — if the fard is invalid, the sunnah performed after it is also invalid.

Imagine you pray Isha without realizing you were not in a state of wudu, then you pray the sunnah and witr with wudu. Later you remember the mistake. Which prayers are valid? The Hanafi school, based on Abu Hanifa, holds that the sunnah is a follower of the fard, so it is invalid and must be repeated. Witr, however, is independent and remains valid due to forgetfulness of the order. This lesson unpacks this ruling and the intra-madhhab disagreement with the two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of prayers
The person prayed Isha (without wudu), then performed wudu, then prayed the sunnah (2 rak'ahs after Isha) and witr with wudu.
2
Apply the follower principle for the sunnah
The sunnah rawatib after the fard is a follower (tabi'). Since the fard was invalid due to lack of wudu, the sunnah performed after it is also invalid, even if performed with wudu. Thus, the sunnah must be repeated.
This applies to any sunnah that is dependent on the fard, typically the rawatib prayed after the fard.
3
Analyze witr's independence and forgetfulness
According to Abu Hanifa, witr is an independent wajib prayer, not a follower of Isha. Although order is generally required between fard and witr, the person performed witr under the impression that Isha was valid. This forgetfulness removes the obligation of order, making witr valid.
The Sahibayn disagree, considering witr a sunnah and thus a follower.
4
Note the exception for tight time
If the time for the current prayer is so tight that only the current fard can be performed, the obligation to make up the invalid prayers (Isha and sunnah) is suspended.
This is a separate principle: diq al-waqt allows prioritization of the current fard.
5
Understand the intra-madhhab disagreement
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that witr is a sunnah and thus a follower of Isha, so it must also be repeated. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's: witr is independent and not repeated.
The practical difference: according to the Sahibayn, all three prayers (Isha, sunnah, witr) are repeated; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only Isha and sunnah are repeated.

(Except when time is tight) [1] His statement: 'he remembers' means the remembering during the time of Isha, because the sunnah is not made up after its time. Therefore the author said: 'and he repeats'. 'Repetition' (i'adah) is defined as performing a second time. They defined 'performance' (ada') as doing the wajib in its time, and 'make-up' (qada') as doing the wajib after its time. Some say: doing the like in other than its time. This is based on the obligation of make-up due to a new cause, while the first is based on obligation by what obligated the performance. And 'repetition' is doing the like of the wajib in its time due to a defect other than invalidity. Some say: doing like the first act in a complete manner. For details of these definitions and others, refer to 'Tahrir al-Usul' by Ibn al-Humam and its commentaries and other usul books. [2] His statement: 'because' is the reason for his saying 'the sunnah was not valid'; meaning the performance of the sunnah was not valid even though he performed it with wudu, because the sunnah is a follower of the fard and is performed after its performance. Since the fard was not effectively performed, the sunnah was not performed either, so its repetition is necessary when repeating the fard. [3] His statement: 'independent' means not following Isha prayer, because it is obligatory according to him, even though its performance is conditioned upon the performance of Isha. (4) His statement: 'he was' meaning he forgot at the time of performing witr that Isha was due upon him. He only remembered that it was without wudu after witr. By forgetfulness, the obligation of order falls, as will come. (0) His statement: 'when it tightens' meaning at the start. So if he starts while remembering the missed prayer at the beginning of the time and prolongs the recitation, i.e., if time becomes tight, it is not permissible. This is stated by Qadi Khan. [6] His statement: 'the time' – does it mean the preferred time or the original time? There are two opinions. [1] Al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir Sharh al-Tahrir (2:123).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a person prays Isha without wudu, and then prays the sunnah and witr with wudu. The ruling: He must repeat Isha and the sunnah, but not witr according to Abu Hanifa. The reason is that the sunnah prayer is a follower (tarba') of the fard prayer. If the fard is invalid due to lack of wudu, then the sunnah performed after it is also invalid, even if performed with wudu, because the sunnah is dependent on the fard. However, witr according to Abu Hanifa is an independent prayer, not a follower of Isha. Even though order is required between witr and Isha, in this case, when he performed witr, he was under the impression that Isha was valid, and he forgot that it was without wudu. Therefore, the obligation of order is waived due to forgetfulness. So witr is valid and need not be repeated. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), witr is a sunnah and thus should also be repeated because it is like other sunnahs that follow the fard. The exception 'except when time is tight' means that if the time for the current prayer is so narrow that there is only enough time to perform the current fard, then the obligation to make up the missed Isha and sunnah is suspended. The commentary on 'time' discusses whether it refers to the preferred time or the core time, with two opinions. The passage also provides definitions of 'ada', 'qada', and 'i'adah' from usul al-fiqh, tying the ruling to broader principles.

Key Terms
التابع (al-tabi'): The follower; the sunnah prayer that is dependent on and follows the fard prayer.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repetition of a prayer in its time due to a defect; here used for repeating Isha and sunnah.
ضيق الوقت (diq al-waqt): The tightness of time such that only the current fard can be performed, excusing the make-up of missed prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which prayers must he repeat if he prayed Isha without wudu, then prayed sunnah and witr with wudu?
A) Only Isha
B) Isha and the sunnah
C) Isha, sunnah, and witr
D) Only the sunnah

Key Takeaway
When a fard prayer is invalid, the sunnah that follows it is also invalid; however, witr is independent and remains valid due to forgetfulness of order.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Ruling on Repeating Prayers When Forgetting Wudu and Exceptions for Time and Forgetfulness
Explains the ruling on repeating prayers when wudu was forgotten and exceptions for time constraint and forgetfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on repeating prayers when wudu was forgotten, distinguish the status of witr according to the three imams, and identify the two exceptions that lift the obligation of tartib.

Core Idea
The sunnah follows the fard; if the fard is invalid, the sunnah is invalid. But witr is independent for Abu Hanifa.

This lesson dives into a common scenario: you pray Isha without wudu (invalid), then pray its sunnah and witr with wudu. Later, you remember. What must be repeated? The answer depends on a key principle: the sunnah is dependent on the fard, so it must be repeated. But witr is different — according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it stands on its own. We will also explore two exceptions that can remove the obligation to pray in order: when time is tight or due to forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the core issue
The passage begins with a scenario: a person prays Isha without wudu, then prays the sunnah and witr with wudu, and then remembers. The question: which prayers must be repeated and why? Identify the act and the ruling sought.
The key is that the fard (Isha) was invalid from the start due to missing wudu.
2
Apply the principle of dependence (taba'iyyah)
The commentator explains that the sunnah is dependent on the fard (tabi'). Since the fard was invalid, the sunnah performed after it—even with valid wudu—is also invalid and must be repeated. This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of sunnah as a follower of the fard.
This principle applies to any sunnah that is explicitly tied to a fard prayer.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on witr
Witr is treated differently. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that witr is an independent wajib prayer, not a sunnah dependent on Isha. Therefore, even though the order (tartib) between Isha and witr was required, forgetfulness at the time of witr (thinking Isha was valid) removed that obligation, leaving witr valid. The two disciples (Sahibayn) consider witr a sunnah, so they require its repetition. Understand the basis of each view.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Define i'ada, ada, and qada
The passage digresses to define technical terms: ada (performing the wajib in its time), qada (after its time), i'ada (repeating an act in its time due to a defect). These definitions clarify that the repetition required here is i'ada, not qada, because the person remembers within the time of Isha.
Hanafis distinguish i'ada from qada; i'ada is only valid within the same prayer time.
5
Examine the exceptions: time constraint and forgetfulness
The main text states that the obligation of order (tartib) is lifted in two cases: (1) when time is tight (diiq al-waqt) — meaning the remaining time cannot accommodate both the make-up and the current prayer; (2) forgetfulness (nisyan) — a heavenly excuse. The commentator elaborates that tartib is only binding if one remembers and has sufficient time. If time is tight, the current prayer takes precedence because its obligation is established by decisive evidence (Book, Sunnah, Ijma), while tartib is based on ahad reports.
The majority of mashayikh interpret 'time' as the original time, not the recommended time.

Source Text

إلا إذا ضاق الوقت يعني تذكر أنه صلى العشاء بلا وضوء والسنة والوتر بوضوء، يعيد العشاءَ والسنة ؛ لأنه لم يصح أداء السنّة مع أنّها أُديت بالوضوء ؛ لأنها تبع للفرض ، أما الوتر فصلاة مستقلة عنده، فصح أداؤه ؛ لأن الترتيب وإن كان فرضا بينه وبين العشاء، لكنه أدى الوتر بزعم أنه صلى العشاء بالوضوء، فكان ناسياً أن العشاء كان في ذمته ، فسقط الترتيب، وعندهما يقضي الوتر أيضاً ؛ لأنَّه سُنَّةٌ عندهما. (إلا إذا ضاق الوقت) قوله : يعني تذكر ; المراد به التذكر في وقتِ العشاء، فإنّ السنَّةَ لا تقضى بعد الوقت، ولذا قال المصنف له : « ويعيد». فإنّ الإعادة عبارة عن أدائه مرة ثانية، وعرَّفوا الأداء بأنه فعلُ الواجب في وقته والقضاء بأنه فعل الواجب بعد وقته، وقيل: فعل مثله في غير وقته، وهذا مبني على وجوب القضاء بسبب جديد، والأول مبني على وجوبه بما يجب به الأداء. والإعادة بأنـه فـعـل لمثل الواجب في وقته ; لخلل غير الفساد، وقيل : الإتيان بمثل الفعل الأول على صفة الكمال، وليطلب تفصيل هذه التعريفات مع تعريفات أُخر من «تحرير الأصول» لابن الهمام وشروحه وغيرها من كتب الأصول. قوله : لأنه ; علّة لقوله : «لم يصح» ; يعني لم يصح أداء السنة وإن صلاها بوضوء ; لأنَّ السنّة تبع للفرض، وتؤدى بعد أدائه، فإذا لم يتأد الفرضُ لم تتأد السنة ، فتلزم إعادتها عند إعادة الفرض. قوله : مستقلة ; أي غير تابعة لصلاة العشاء; لأنها واجبة عنده، وإن كان أداؤها مشروطاً بأداء العشاء. قوله : فكان ; أي نسي عند أداء الوتر كون العشاء في ذمته، فإنه إنما تذكره كونه بغير الوضوء بعد الوتر، وبالنسيان تسقط فرضيّة الترتيب كما سيأتي. قوله : إذا ضاق ; أي عند الشروع ، فلو شرع مع تذكر الفائتة في أول الوقت وأطال القراءة، أي إن ضاق الوقت لا يجوز، كذا ذكره قاضي خان. قوله : الوقت ; هل المراد به المستحب أم أصل الوقت، فيه قولان: والذي عليه أكثر المشايخ هو اعتبار الثاني، وهو ظاهرُ المتون، والأول رواية عن محمد الله.
أو نسيت (الاستثناء) متصل بقوله : فرضُ التَّرتيب ، والمعنى أنه ضاق الوقت عن القضاء والأداء، وإن كان الباقي من الوقت بحيث يسعُ فيه بعض الفوائتِ مع الوقتية فإنَّه يقضى ما يسعه الوقتُ مع الوقتية، كما إذا فات العشاء والوتر، ولم يبقَ من وقت الفجر إلا أن يسع خمس ركعات يقضي الوتر، ويؤدي الفجر عند أبي حنيفة ، وإن فات الظهر والعصر، ولم يبق من وقتِ المغرب إلا ما يسع سبع ركعات يُصَلِّي الظهر والمغرب. قوله : متصل ... الخ; والمعنى فرض الترتيب في جميع الأحوال، إلا عند ضيق الوقت، فحينئذ لا يبقى فرضا. قوله : والمعنى.. الخ ; فإذا لم يكن في الوقتِ أن يؤدّي القضاء والأداء كليهما يترك القضاء ويُصلّى الأداء ; لأنّ فرض الوقت أكد من فرض الترتيب ; ولأن فرض الوقت في الوقتيّة ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وفرضُ الترتيب إنما ثبت بأخبار الآحاد. قوله : ما يسعه ; أي يؤدّي الفائتة التي يمكن أن يؤديها مع الوقتية. قوله : يقضي الوتر... الخ ; ظاهر كلام أكثرهم أن الوقت إذا وسع الوقتية وبعض الفوائت يلزم عليه أن يُصلي ما وسعه مقدّماً للفائتة على الوقتية ; لأنَّ فرضَ الترتيب إنما يسقط بعذر الضيق، فيتقدّر بقدره، لكن صرّح في «المجتبى» وغيره : أن الأصح أنه لو صلّى الوقتية في هذه الصورة وترك جميع الفوائت جاز. قوله : يصلي الظهر... الخ ; فلا بد أن يقضي من الفوائت ما يمكن قضاؤه ، مع عدم تفويت الوقتيّة، فإن أمكنه الترتيب فيما بينهما أيضاً راعاه. قوله : أو نسيت ; بصيغة المجهول والضمير إلى الفائتة، وإنّما سقط فرضُ الترتيب بالنسيان ; لأنه عذر سماوي، فهو معذور فيه ، فلو صلّى الوقتية أولاً ناسياً أنّ عليه قضاء جازت صلاته، فإذا تذكر يؤدي الفائتة. وهو استثناء من لزوم الترتيب ، فلا يلزم الترتيب إذا ضاق الوقت
Except when time is tight (meaning he remembers that he prayed Isha without wudu, and the sunnah and witr with wudu, he repeats Isha and the sunnah because the sunnah was not validly performed even though it was performed with wudu because it is dependent on the obligatory prayer. As for witr, it is an independent prayer according to him (Abu Hanifa), so its performance was valid; because the order (tartib), even though it is obligatory between it and Isha, but he performed witr under the impression that he had prayed Isha with wudu, so he was forgetful that Isha was still incumbent upon him, so the obligation of order falls away. According to the two disciples, he also repeats witr because it is a sunnah according to them. (Except when time is tight) He said: meaning he remembers; what is meant is remembering during the time of Isha, for the sunnah is not made up after the time, hence the author said for him: 'and he repeats'. Indeed, 'repetition' (i'ada) is the performance of something a second time, and they defined 'performance' (ada) as doing the obligatory in its time, and 'make-up' (qada) as doing the obligatory after its time, and it was said: doing its like outside its time, and this is based on the obligation of make-up due to a new cause, whereas the first is based on its obligation being by the same cause as the performance. And 'repetition' is doing the like of the obligatory in its time due to a defect not amounting to invalidity, and it was said: performing the first act in a perfect manner. And the detail of these definitions along with other definitions should be sought from 'Tahrir al-Usul' of Ibn al-Humam and its commentaries and other books of usul. He said: because; it is the reason for his statement: 'was not valid'; meaning the sunnah was not valid even though he prayed it with wudu because the sunnah is dependent on the obligatory (fard), and is performed after its performance; so if the obligatory was not validly performed, the sunnah is not validly performed, so its repetition is necessary when repeating the obligatory. He said: independent; meaning not dependent on the Isha prayer because it is obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa), even though its performance is conditioned by the performance of Isha. He said: so he was; meaning he forgot at the time of performing witr that Isha was still incumbent upon him; indeed he only remembered that it was without wudu after witr, and due to forgetfulness the obligation of order falls away as will come. He said: when it is tight; meaning at the start; so if he starts while remembering the missed prayer at the beginning of the time and prolongs the recitation, meaning if time becomes tight, it is not permissible, as mentioned by Qadi Khan. He said: the time; whether what is meant is the recommended time or the original time, there are two sayings; and the one held by most mashayikh is the second, and it is the apparent meaning of the texts, and the first is a narration from Muhammad. Or she forgot (the exception) is connected to his statement: the obligation of order, and the meaning is that time is too tight for both make-up and performance, and if the remaining time is such that it can accommodate some of the missed prayers together with the current prayer, then he makes up what the time allows together with the current prayer, as in the case where Isha and witr are missed, and there remains of the time of Fajr only so much that it can accommodate five rak'ahs: he prays witr and performs Fajr according to Abu Hanifa; and if Zuhr and Asr are missed, and there remains of the time of Maghrib only so much that it can accommodate seven rak'ahs: he prays Zuhr and Maghrib. He said: connected... etc.; and the meaning: the obligation of order applies in all circumstances except when time is tight; then it does not remain obligatory. He said: and the meaning... etc.; so if there is not in the time to perform both make-up and performance, he abandons the make-up and prays the current prayer because the obligation of the current time is stronger than the obligation of order; and because the obligation of the current prayer in its time is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, whereas the obligation of order is only established by ahad reports. He said: what accommodates it; meaning he performs the missed prayer that he can perform together with the current prayer. He said: prays witr... etc.; the apparent meaning of the majority is that when the time accommodates the current prayer and some of the missed prayers, it is incumbent upon him to pray what accommodates, giving precedence to the missed prayer over the current prayer because the obligation of order is only removed by the excuse of tightness, so it is restricted to its extent. But it is stated in al-Mujtaba and others: that the more correct view is that if he prayed the current prayer in this situation and left all the missed prayers, it is permissible. He said: prays Zuhr... etc.; so it is necessary that he makes up from the missed prayers what he can make up without causing the loss of the current prayer; and if it is possible to observe order between them, he also observes it. He said: or she forgot; in the passive voice, and the pronoun refers to the missed prayer, and the obligation of order falls only due to forgetfulness because it is a heavenly excuse, so he is excused in it; thus, if he prayed the current prayer first, forgetting that he had a make-up upon him, his prayer is valid, and when he remembers he performs the missed prayer. And it is an exception from the binding nature of order, so order is not binding when time is tight.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi commentary (sharh) on a matn concerning the rules of make-up prayers (qada al-fawa'it). The author expands on the ruling when one remembers having prayed a fard prayer (Isha) without wudu, but after having prayed the sunnah and witr with wudu. The ruling is that the fard (Isha) and its attached sunnah must be repeated. The sunnah is a dependent act (tabi'), so if the fard it follows is invalid, the sunnah is also invalid even if its own conditions (like wudu) were met. Witr, however, is different: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, witr is an independent prayer (wajib), not a sunnah dependent on Isha, so if one performed it under the impression that Isha was valid, the order requirement (tartib) fell due to forgetfulness, and witr stands valid. The two disciples (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) consider witr a sunnah, so they require its repetition as well. The passage then discusses definitions of ada (performance in time), qada (make-up after time), and i'ada (repetition in time due to a defect). The main exception to the obligatoriness of order (tartib) is when time is tight: if the remaining time cannot accommodate both the make-up and the current prayer, the current prayer takes precedence because it is established by decisive evidence (Quran, mutawatir sunnah, ijma), whereas order is only based on ahad reports. If there is enough time for some but not all missed prayers, one must prioritize what can be made up without losing the current prayer, according to the majority. However, al-Mujtaba states the more correct view is that one may pray the current prayer even if it means abandoning all make-ups. Forgetfulness (nisyan) is another valid excuse: if one prays the current prayer forgetting about a make-up, the prayer is valid, and he must make up the missed prayer later. The passage emphasizes that tartib is binding only when one remembers and has sufficient time.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'ada): Repeating the same obligatory prayer in its time due to a defect that does not amount to invalidity of the original act.
ترتيب (tartib): The obligation of performing prayers in sequence when praying both fard and make-up prayers; order must be maintained unless an excuse exists.
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetfulness that excuses the requirement of tartib; it is considered a 'heavenly excuse' (udhr samawi).
ضيق الوقت (diiq al-waqt): Time constraint that prevents performing both the missed prayer and the current prayer within the current prayer's time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for lifting the obligation of tartib (order) between missed and current prayers?
A) Time is too tight to perform both
B) Forgetfulness about the missed prayer
C) The missed prayer is witr
D) The current prayer time is about to end

Key Takeaway
The sunnah depends on the fard; if the fard is invalid, the sunnah is invalid. Witr is independent per Abu Hanifa. Time constraint and forgetfulness lift the obligation of order between make-up and current prayers.

Exception of Tight Time for Qada Prayers
Explains when the obligation of order is dropped due to lack of time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the obligation of order (tartib) for missed prayers and identify when it is dropped due to tight time or forgetfulness.

Core Idea
When time is too short for both qada and ada, the order obligation drops — the present prayer takes precedence.

The Hanafi school holds that performing missed prayers in order before the present prayer is wajib, based on ahad hadith. However, this obligation is not absolute. When the remaining time cannot accommodate both the missed and the present prayer, the order requirement is lifted. The present prayer, being established by definitive proofs, takes priority. This lesson unpacks the exception, including scenarios where partial time exists and the effect of forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The obligation of order (tartib) means missed prayers must be made up before the present prayer in the order they were missed. The Hanafi classifies this as wajib.
Not fard because the evidence is zanni (ahad hadith).
2
Understand the epistemic basis
The order obligation is based on ahad reports, making it weaker than the present prayer's obligation (Quran, mutawatir sunna, ijma). Hence it can be overridden.
This is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Recognize the exception for tight time
When the remaining time cannot accommodate both the missed and the present prayer, order is no longer required. One prays the present only.
Exception is limited to the extent of necessity.
4
Apply to partial time scenario
If time allows some missed prayers along with the present, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa says make up what you can before the present; the preferred view (al-Mujtaba) permits praying the present first and leaving all missed.
The mufta bihi is the permissive view.
5
Include forgetfulness as an exception
Forgetfulness of the missed prayer also drops the order. If one prays the present forgetting the qada, the prayer is valid; one then makes up the missed later.
Forgetfulness is a heavenly excuse.

Source Text

This is an exception to the necessity of order, so order is not obligatory when time is tight.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the exception to the obligation of order in making up missed prayers. The core rule: the obligation of order (tartib) between missed and present prayers is obligatory in general, but is dropped when time is too short to accommodate both. The author explains that if there is not enough time to perform both the missed (qada) and the present (ada) prayers, one prioritizes the present prayer because its obligation is stronger—being established by definitive evidence (Quran, mutawatir sunna, consensus) whereas the order obligation is based on ahad hadiths. If time allows for some missed prayers along with the present, there is a difference: the majority view (based on the principle that the excuse is limited to the extent of necessity) obligates making up as many as possible before the present prayer. But some, as in al-Mujtaba, hold that it is permissible to pray the present first and leave all missed prayers. The author also covers forgetfulness: if one forgets the missed prayer and prays the present first, it is valid, and then he must make up the missed when he remembers. The passage ends by reiterating that tightness of time is an exemption from the order obligation.

Key Terms
ضاق الوقت (Ḍāqa al-waqt): The situation where the remaining time for the present prayer is insufficient to perform both the missed prayer(s) and the present prayer.
فرض الترتيب (Farḍ al-tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in the order they were missed and before the present prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the obligation of order (tartib) between missed and present prayers dropped?
A) Only when the missed prayers are six or more.
B) When time is too short to perform both the missed and present prayer, or due to forgetfulness.
C) Never; order is always obligatory.
D) Only for women.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of order for missed prayers is wajib but has two Hanafi exceptions: tight time and forgetfulness, both prioritizing the present prayer.

The Exception of Six Missed Prayers: When Order Is Dropped
Expansion of the exception for six missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi threshold for dropping the obligation of order among missed fard prayers and apply the exception to determine whether order is required in a given scenario.

Core Idea
When missed fard prayers reach six, the obligation of ordering them is waived to remove hardship.

This lesson examines the second major exception to the rule of order among prayers. The Hanafi school holds that if a person accumulates six or more missed fard prayers, the duty to pray them in sequence is dropped, whether the missed prayers are recent or old. The passage also clarifies that Witr is not counted toward this number.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exception
The obligation of order (tartib) between prayers is normally wajib. The passage discusses the exception when the number of missed fard prayers reaches six.
This exception is based on the principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship).
2
Determine the threshold: six missed fard prayers
Count only fard prayers (not Witr). When the count is six or more, order is no longer required.
Witr is excluded because it is not a fard, and its inclusion would not create the required numerousness.
3
Distinguish between recent and old
The text explicitly states that the exception covers both recent (haditha) and old (qadima) missed prayers, according to the relied-upon view.
Some limited opinions restrict it to recent, but the mufta bihi is absolute.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Muhammad al-Shaybani considered the entry of the time of the sixth prayer as the trigger, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf considered the accumulation of six prayers alone.
The correct view per al-Hidaya is accumulation, because numerousness occurs by crossing the threshold of six.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a set of missed prayers, decide if order is required. For example, if a person missed 6 Fajr prayers, he may pray any present prayer without making them up first.
The fatwa is based on al-Kafi and al-Muhit.

قوله : أو فاتت سنة حديثة كانت أو قديمة ) ، قيل : السنة وما دونها حديثة، وما فوقها كثيرة ) [١]قوله : أو فاتت ستة ؛ يعني لا يلزم الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية، ولا بين الفوائت إذا كانت الفوائت ستاً، والمراد بالفوائت هاهنا الفرائض الاعتقادية، فيخرج الوتر، فإنّ الترتيب بينه وبين غيره وإن كان فرضاً، لكنّه لا يحسب مع الفوائت ؛ لأنه لا تحصل به الكثرة المفضية إلى السقوط ؛ لأنه من تمام وظيفة اليوم والليلة، والكثرة لا تحصل إلا بالزيادة عليها من حيث الأوقات أو من حيث الساعات، ولا مدخل للوتر في ذلك (٢). كذا حققه الشرنبلالي. (۲) (٢) قوله : سنّة ؛ أشار إلى أنّ المعتبركون الفوائتِ ستّة، وعن محمد له أنه اعتبر دخول وقت السادسة، والصحيح هو الأوّل ؛ لأنَّ الكثرة بالدخول في حد التكرار، وذلك بالأول. كذا في «الهداية»(۳). [٣] قوله : حديثة كانت أو قديمة ؛ أي سواء كانت الفوائتُ في الزمان القريب المتصل بأداء الوقتية، أو في الزمان البعيد، فالحديثة تسقط الترتيب اتفاقاً، دفعاً للحرج، وكذلك القديمة عند البعض، كمن ترك صلوات شهر مثلاً، ثمّ صلّى مدة الصلاة في أوقاتها، ولم تقض تلك الصلاة حتى ترك الصلاة، ثمّ صلّى أخرى وقتيّة ذاكراً لتلك الحديثة، تجوز صلاته، وعند البعض لا والفتوى على الأوّل. كذا يفهم من «الكافي» و«المحيط»، وهو الذي اختاره المصنف الله ، والحاصل أنّ الفوائت إذا صارت ستّاً سقط الترتيب مطلقاً، ـواء كانت كلّها قديمة أو كلّها حديثة، أو بعضها قديمة وبعضها حديثة. ، سوا [٤] قوله : قيل....الخ ؛ ذهب بعض الناظرين إلى أن الغرض من هذا الكلام الطعنُ على المصنف له بأنه مشى في التعبير بالحديثة والقديمة، وتقسيمه الستة إليهما على خلاف اصطلاح الفقهاء، من أن الستة وما دونها حديثة وما زاد عليها قديمة، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن المقصود منه تضعيف تلك الرواية، وترجيح ما ذكره المصنف ؛ ولذا
His statement: 'Or if six (missed prayers) are missed, whether recent or old.' It is said: six and below are recent, and above that are many. [1] His statement: 'Or if six are missed' means that order is not obligatory between the missed and the present prayer, nor between the missed prayers themselves if the missed prayers number six. What is meant here by 'missed prayers' are the obligatory (fard) prayers, so Witr is excluded. For the order between it and others is indeed obligatory, but it is not counted among the missed prayers because it does not bring about the numerousness (kathra) that leads to dropping the order, since it is part of the complete daily and nightly function, and numerousness is only achieved by an increase beyond that in terms of timings or hours, and Witr has no role in that. This is as verified by Shurunbulali. (2) His statement: 'Six' indicates that the considered number of missed prayers is six. From Muhammad it is reported that he considered the entry of the time of the sixth prayer. The correct view is the first, because numerousness occurs by entering into the threshold of repetition, and that is with the first. This is in al-Hidaya. [3] His statement: 'Whether recent or old' i.e., whether the missed prayers are in the near time connected to the performance of the present prayer, or in the distant past. Recent ones drop the order by agreement, to remove hardship; similarly, old ones according to some. For example, a person who missed prayers of a month, then prayed for a while at their proper times without making up those missed, then prays another present prayer while remembering those recent missed ones, his prayer is permissible. According to others it is not, and the fatwa is on the first view. This is understood from al-Kafi and al-Muhit, and it is what the author chose. The conclusion: when the missed prayers reach six, order is dropped absolutely, whether all are old, all recent, or some old and some recent. [4] His statement: 'It is said...' etc. Some commentators held that the purpose of this statement is to criticize the author for using the terms 'recent' and 'old' and dividing the six into them contrary to the jurists' terminology (six and below are recent, above are old). Others held that the purpose is to weaken that narration and to prefer what the author mentioned; hence...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage expands on the second major exception to the obligation of order: when one has missed six or more fard prayers. The commentator clarifies that the number six refers to obligatory prayers only—Witr is excluded because it is not a fard prayer but wajib, and its inclusion would not count toward the numerousness. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: Muhammad al-Shaybani considered the entry of the time of the sixth missed prayer as the threshold, but the correct view (as in al-Hidaya) is that crossing the threshold of six accumulated missed prayers is the trigger. The passage also addresses the distinction between 'recent' (haditha) and 'old' (qadima) missed prayers. The ruling: when six are missed, the order is dropped absolutely—whether they are all recent, all old, or mixed. Some scholars argued about the use of terminology, but the author's position is that once six are missed, order is no longer required for any of them. The practical scenario given: a person missed many prayers over a month, then prayed for a while at proper times without making them up, then remembered the recent ones while praying a present prayer—the prayer is valid, and he need not repeat it in order. This is the fatwa according to al-Kafi and al-Muhit.

Key Terms
ستة (Sitta): The number of missed obligatory prayers that triggers the dropping of the order obligation; six or more.
حديثة (Ḥadītha): Missed prayers that are recent, i.e., within the timeframe of the present prayer or near to it.
قديمة (Qadīma): Missed prayers from the distant past, such as those from months ago.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many missed fard prayers must one have for the obligation of order to be dropped?
A) Three
B) Six
C) Five
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
When the number of missed fard prayers reaches six, the obligation of order is dropped absolutely, whether the missed prayers are recent or old, and Witr is not counted.

Salah — Prayer

Six Missed Prayers Lift the Order Requirement
Rule that six missed prayers lift order obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that six missed prayers lift the tartib obligation and apply it to scenarios involving recent and old missed prayers.

Core Idea
Six missed prayers lift the order requirement, regardless of recency — hardship removal is the basis.

Praying missed prayers in order (tartib) is normally obligatory. But when does this obligation drop? The Hanafi school provides a clear threshold: six missed prayers. In this lesson, we examine the ruling from Al-Wiqayah and its commentary, understand the rationale of hardship removal, and distinguish between recent and old missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that if six obligatory prayers (fara'id) are missed, the requirement for tartib — both between missed prayers and between missed and current prayers — is lifted. This is a clear rule derived from the principle of removing hardship.
Note: Witr is excluded from the count because it is not a full obligatory prayer in the same sense; it is part of the daily routine.
2
Understand the criterion: count vs. time
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the mere count of six missed prayers suffices to lift tartib. Muhammad al-Shaybani requires the entry of the time of the sixth prayer. The relied-upon (sahih) position is Abu Hanifa's, as confirmed in Al-Hidayah.
The rationale: multiplicity (kathrah) leading to hardship is achieved by the count itself, not by the passage of time.
3
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The basis for this rule is the removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj). When missed prayers accumulate, requiring order would cause severe difficulty. Islamic law eases such burdens. The number six is the threshold determined by the early jurists based on customary practice.
The proof is not a specific textual command but a general principle (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir).
4
Differentiate 'jadidah' and 'qadimah'
The text clarifies that both recent missed prayers (connected to the current time) and old missed prayers (distant in time) trigger the lifting of order. Once the count of six is reached, the rule applies absolutely, regardless of whether all are recent, all old, or a mix.
This removes any ambiguity about time gaps; the focus is purely on the number.
5
Apply to a sample scenario
Consider someone who missed all prayers of one month (e.g., 30 prayers), then later remembers and starts praying current prayers. He also misses one more prayer today. His current prayer is valid without making up the missed ones in order, because the old missed prayers already exceeded six and lifted the order.
This scenario is mentioned in Al-Kafi and Al-Muhit, and the fatwa agrees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو فاتت سنة حديثة كانت أو قديمة
[1]قوله : أو فاتت ستة ؛ يعني لا يلزم الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية، ولا بين الفوائت إذا كانت الفوائت ستاً، والمراد بالفوائت هاهنا الفرائض الاعتقادية، فيخرج الوتر، فإنّ الترتيب بينه وبين غيره وإن كان فرضاً، لكنّه لا يحسب مع الفوائت ؛ لأنه لا تحصل به الكثرة المفضية إلى السقوط ؛ لأنه من تمام وظيفة اليوم والليلة، والكثرة لا تحصل إلا بالزيادة عليها من حيث الأوقات أو من حيث الساعات، ولا مدخل للوتر في ذلك. كذا حققه الشرنبلالي.
(2) قوله : سنّة ؛ أشار إلى أنّ المعتبركون الفوائتِ ستّة، وعن محمد له أنه اعتبر دخول وقت السادسة، والصحيح هو الأوّل ؛ لأنَّ الكثرة بالدخول في حد التكرار، وذلك بالأول. كذا في «الهداية».
[3] قوله : حديثة كانت أو قديمة ؛ أي سواء كانت الفوائتُ في الزمان القريب المتصل بأداء الوقتية، أو في الزمان البعيد، فالحديثة تسقط الترتيب اتفاقاً، دفعاً للحرج، وكذلك القديمة عند البعض، كمن ترك صلوات شهر مثلاً، ثمّ صلّى مدة الصلاة في أوقاتها، ولم تقض تلك الصلاة حتى ترك الصلاة، ثمّ صلّى أخرى وقتيّة ذاكراً لتلك الحديثة، تجوز صلاته، وعند البعض لا والفتوى على الأوّل. كذا يفهم من «الكافي» و«المحيط»، وهو الذي اختاره المصنف الله ، والحاصل أنّ الفوائت إذا صارت ستّاً سقط الترتيب مطلقاً، سواء كانت كلّها قديمة أو كلّها حديثة، أو بعضها قديمة وبعضها حديثة.
or if six [prayers] are missed, whether recent or old. [1] He said: 'or if six are missed' means that order is not required between the missed and the current prayer, nor among missed prayers if the missed prayers are six. What is meant by missed prayers here are the obligatory prayers that are firmly established, thus witr is excluded. For although order between it [witr] and other [prayers] is obligatory, it is not counted among the missed [prayers], because multiplicity leading to abrogation is not attained by it; it is part of the complete function of the day and night, and multiplicity is only attained by exceeding it in terms of times or hours, and witr has no part in that. Thus verified by al-Shurunbulali. (2) He said: 'sunnah'; he indicated that the criterion for [the count of] missed prayers is six. And from Muhammad [al-Shaybani] that he considered the entry of the time of the sixth [prayer], and the correct is the first, because multiplicity is by entering into the limit of repetition, and that is by the first. Thus in al-Hidayah. [3] He said: 'whether recent or old' meaning whether the missed prayers are in the near time connected to the performance of the current prayer, or in the distant time. The recent ones abrogate order by agreement, to remove hardship, and likewise the old ones according to some, such as one who missed prayers of a month, for example, then prayed for a period during their times, and did not make up those prayers until he abandoned prayer, then prayed another time-based [prayer] while mindful of those recent ones – his prayer is permissible. And according to some, no. The fatwa is on the first. Thus understood from al-Kafi and al-Muhit, and that is what the author chose. The conclusion: when missed prayers become six, order is abrogated absolutely, whether all are old, all are new, or some are old and some new.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Al-Wiqayah. It states that if a person has missed six obligatory prayers (not including witr), the requirement to pray them in order (tartib) is lifted, both between missed prayers themselves and between missed and current prayers. The rationale (dalil aqli) is that a large number creates hardship (haraj), and Islamic law removes hardship. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Some, like Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider the entry of the sixth prayer's time as the criterion, but the relied-upon position (as in al-Hidayah) is that the count of six is enough, regardless of time. The term 'jadidah' (recent) and 'qadimah' (old) are defined: recent means in continuous time with the current prayer; old means distant in time. Both types lift the order requirement once six are missed. An example: one who missed a month of prayers, then started praying current prayers, then missed another prayer – his current prayer is valid because the old missed prayers (the month) already removed the order.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation to pray missed prayers in the order they were missed, and to pray current prayers after missed ones.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers (excluding witr in this context).
حديثة (jadidah): Recent missed prayers, connected in time to the current prayer.
قديمة (qadimah): Old missed prayers, distant in time from the current prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has missed exactly six obligatory prayers. According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on tartib?
A) He must pray them in order before the current prayer.
B) He may pray the current prayer without order.
C) He must perform sajdah al-sahw if he prays current prayer without order.
D) He must combine the missed prayers with the current prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that six missed obligatory prayers (excluding witr) lift the obligation of tartib, regardless of whether they are recent or old, based on the principle of removing hardship.

Definitions of 'New' and 'Old' Missed Prayers and Their Effect on Tartib
Analysis of the meaning of 'jadidah' and 'qadimah' and their impact on the ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on the classification of missed prayers and apply the ruling that six missed prayers lift the obligation of order, regardless of terminology.

Core Idea
Six missed prayers lift the order—whether called 'new' or 'old', the ruling is absolute.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute over the precise meanings of 'jadidah' (new) and 'qadimah' (old) in the context of missed prayers. Some scholars criticized the author of al-Hidayah for using these terms contrary to the standard Hanafi convention, but the commentators defend him, showing that the essential ruling—that six or more missed prayers negate the obligation of order—remains unchanged regardless of terminology. Through examples from al-Nihaya and al-Muhit, the lesson clarifies that the classification is academic, not practical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed point
What exactly is contested? The definition of 'jadidah' and 'qadimah': is it based on number (six or fewer vs more than six) or on temporal proximity to the current prayer? This affects whether the obligation of order is lifted.
The dispute is about terminology, but it has a practical consequence when the number of missed prayers is exactly six.
2
State the two positions
Position 1 (the critics): six and fewer are 'new', more than six are 'old'. Position 2 (the author and preferred view): 'new' means temporally close, 'old' means distant; the ruling applies whenever six or more are missed, regardless of label.
Both sides are Hanafi, but the second view is mufta bihi.
3
Analyze the evidence
The critics rely on conventional juristic usage. The author and his defenders rely on rational proof (avoiding hardship) and examples from al-Nihaya and al-Muhit: a month's worth of missed prayers (old) lift the order, and the same applies even if the missed prayers are from the same day (new).
The examples show that the ruling is not bound by the number-based definition.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? If someone misses six prayers from the same day, according to the critics (who call them 'new'), the order must be observed; according to the preferred view, the order is lifted and he may pray the current prayer first.
Thus, the disagreement does affect practice in the six-prayer scenario.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The preferred view, as supported by the examples and later commentaries (al-Kafi, al-Muhit, Umda al-Riaya), is that six missed prayers lift the order absolutely. The definitional debate does not change the operative ruling.
The fatwa is on this inclusive view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : قيل....الخ ; ذهب بعض الناظرين إلى أن الغرض من هذا الكلام الطعنُ على المصنف له بأنه مشى في التعبير بالحديثة والقديمة، وتقسيمه الستة إليهما على خلاف اصطلاح الفقهاء، من أن الستة وما دونها حديثة وما زاد عليها قديمة، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن المقصود منه تضعيف تلك الرواية، وترجيح ما ذكره المصنف ; ولذا قلت بعد الكثرة أو لا ، فيصح وقتي من ترك صلاة شهرٍ فَنَدِم ، وأخذ يؤدي الوقتيات ، ثم ترك فرضاً ، أو قضى صلاةَ الشَّهْرِ إلا فرضاً أو فرضين كذا في «فوائد) (الجامع الصغير الحسامي»، (قلت بعد الكثرة أو لا ، فيصح وقتي من ترك صلاة شهرٍ فَنَدِم ، وأخذ يؤدي الوقتيات ، ثم ترك فرضاً)، هذا تفريع قوله : قديمة كانت أو حديثة ، فإنَّه إذا أخذ يؤدي الوقتيات صارت فوائت الشهرِ ،قديمة، وهي مسقطة للترتيب، فإذا ترك فرضاً يجوز مع ذكرِهِ أداء وقتي بعده. [٤] (أو قضى صلاة الشهر إلا فرضاً أو فرضين) عبر عنها بلفظ : قيل، ومنهم من قال : مراده أنّ السنّة وما دونها إذا صارت فاصلة بينك وبين الفائتة، فالفائتة حديثة، وإذا فصل فوق الستة، فالفائتة قديمة. [٣] قوله : فإنه إذا أخذ ... الخ ; قال في «النهاية»: رجل ترك صلاة شهر فسقاً، ثم نَدِمَ على ما صَنَعَ واشتغل بأداء الصلاة في مواقيتها، فالفوائت قديمة، وقبل أن تقضى تلك الفوائت ترك الصلاة ثمّ صلّى صلاة أخرى وهو ذاكر لهذه المتروكة يجوز ; لأن الاشتغال بهذهِ الفائتة ليس بأولى من الاشتغال بتلك الفوائت، والاشتغال بالكل يُفوّت الوقتية عن وقتها. كذا في «المحيط». (٤) قوله : أو قضى...الخ ; قال في «العناية»: «صورته : أن يترك الرجل صلاة شهرٍ ثم يقضيها إلا صلاة أو صلاتين، ثمّ صلّى صلاة دخل وقتها وهو ذاكر لما بقي هل تجوز الوقتية أو لم تجز , فعن محمد الله فيه روايتان ، ومال إلى عدم الجواز الفقيه أبو جعفر (۱) «الفوائد البهية ( ص ٢٤٢). وينظر : «الجواهر المضية) (۲) : (٦٤٩) ، والنجوم الزاهرة» (٥) : ٢٦٨)، وغيرها.
His statement: 'qila' etc. Some of the scholars held that the purpose of this statement is to criticize the author, because he used the terms 'new' and 'old' and divided the six into them contrary to the terminology of the jurists, that six and less are new, and more than six are old. And some held that the intention is to weaken that narration and to prefer what the author mentioned. Hence: 'I said after multiplicity or not, so a time-based prayer is valid from one who missed a month of prayers, then repented, and began to perform the time-based prayers, then missed an obligatory prayer, or made up the prayers of the month except one or two obligatory prayers.' Thus in 'Fawa'id al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami'. (I said after multiplicity or not, so a time-based prayer is valid from one who missed a month of prayers, then repented, and began to perform the time-based prayers, then missed an obligatory prayer) – this is a branch of his statement: 'old or new', because when he began to perform the time-based prayers, the missed prayers of the month became old, and they are abrogating of order. So when he misses an obligatory prayer, it is permissible for him, while mindful of it, to perform a time-based prayer after it. [4] (or he made up the prayers of the month except one or two obligatory prayers) – he expressed this with the word 'qila'. Some of them said: his intent is that when six or less come between you and the missed prayer, then the missed prayer is new; and when more than six separate, then the missed prayer is old. [1] He said: 'in Fawa'id...' it is the commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Husam al-Din al-Sadr al-Shahid, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, d. 536 AH, and I have detailed his biography in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya. [2] He said: 'qultu' means that multiplicity of missed prayers abrogates order absolutely, whether they become few after multiplicity or not. [3] He said: 'for example, if he begins...' – he said in al-Nihaya: A man missed a month's prayers out of disobedience, then repented of what he did and busied himself with performing prayers in their times. Then the missed prayers become old. Before he makes up those missed prayers, he abandons prayer, then prays another prayer while mindful of this abandoned one – it is permissible, because occupying himself with this missed prayer is not more appropriate than occupying himself with those missed prayers, and occupying himself with all would cause the time-based prayer to miss its time. Thus in al-Muhit. (4) He said: 'or he made up...' – he said in al-Inaya: 'Its picture: A man misses a month of prayers, then makes them up except one or two prayers, then prays a prayer whose time has entered while mindful of what remains. Is the time-based prayer valid or not? From Muhammad [al-Shaybani] there are two narrations, and al-Faqih Abu Ja'far inclined to non-permissibility.' (1) al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 242. See also al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya (2):649, and al-Nujum al-Zahira (5):268, etc.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the precise definitions of 'jadidah' (new) and 'qadimah' (old) missed prayers and their effect on the rule that six missed prayers lift the obligation of order (tartib). Some scholars criticize the author for using the terms in a way that contradicts standard Hanafi terminology, where 'new' means six or fewer and 'old' means more than six. Others defend the author, arguing that the criticism itself weakens a certain narration. The passage provides examples: if a person misses a month of prayers, then repents and performs current prayers on time, the missed prayers become 'old' and thus the order is lifted – so if he later misses another prayer, he may pray the current prayer first. Another example: if he makes up all but one or two of the month's prayers, Muhammad al-Shaybani has two narrations on the validity of praying a current prayer before completing the remaining missed prayers; Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani inclined to non-validity. The commentary from al-Nihaya and al-Muhit supports the view that the old missed prayers (even if numerous) lift the order, and the worshipper may choose which to make up first. The key principle is 'multiplicity of missed prayers abrogates order absolutely.'

Key Terms
الحديثة (al-jadidah): Recent missed prayers that are connected in time to the current prayer (e.g., missed on the same day or shortly before).
القديمة (al-qadimah): Old missed prayers that are distant in time (e.g., from a previous month).
قيل (qila): A term used to introduce a critical or alternative viewpoint; here it signals a dispute over terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi) presented in this passage, which of the following is correct regarding a person who has six missed prayers from the same day?
A) He must pray them in order because they are 'new' prayers.
B) He may pray the current prayer before making them up because six missed prayers lift the order.
C) He must make up the six prayers first, but he may choose the order.
D) He may only pray the current prayer after making up all missed prayers.

Key Takeaway
Six or more missed prayers, regardless of being called 'new' or 'old', lift the obligation of order, allowing current prayers to be performed before making them up.

The Validity of Current Prayer When Numerous Missed Prayers Abrogate Order
Ruling on validity of current prayer when numerous missed prayers exist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a large number of missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it) abrogates the requirement of order (tartib) between missed and current prayers, and determine the validity of a current prayer in such cases.

Core Idea
Many missed prayers drop order — a current prayer is valid even if you remember dozens of unpaid prayers.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person has missed many prayers (e.g., a month), repents, and starts praying regularly. While praying a current prayer, he remembers the backlog. Does his prayer become invalid because of the missed order? The Hanafi school provides a merciful concession: when the number of missed prayers is large, the obligation of sequence is lifted, and the current prayer remains valid. This ruling is derived from the principle of necessity and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario involves a person who has missed a large number of obligatory prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it), then repents and begins performing current time-bound prayers regularly. While performing a current prayer, he remembers the missed ones.
The key element is the large number of missed prayers, not just any number.
2
Determine the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the current prayer is valid (sahih) despite the memory of the missed prayers, because the large number of missed prayers abrogates the obligation of order (tartib).
The ruling is explicit: the prayer is valid even if he remembers the missed ones.
3
Understand the reason
The reason is that the missed prayers become 'old' (qadima) when they are numerous. Once they are considered old, they are 'musqitat li al-tartib' (abrogators of order). The requirement to perform them in sequence before the current prayer is dropped.
This is based on the principle that necessity (keeping the current prayer valid) overrides strict sequencing.
4
Distinguish from few missed prayers
If the missed prayers are few (generally 5 or less), order is still required. In that case, the current prayer would be invalid if performed before making up the missed ones. The distinction hinges on the number of missed prayers.
The Hanafi school defines 'kathira' (abundance) as 6 or more missed prayers.
5
Apply to various numbers
If the missed prayers are six or more, they are considered old and order is dropped. If they are five or less, order remains. This ruling applies to any combination of missed prayers, as long as the total is six or more.
This is a settled Hanafi position, though other schools differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

I said: whether after abundance or not, so a time-bound prayer is valid from one who left a month's prayer, then repented, and began performing time-bound prayers, then left an obligatory prayer, or made up the month's prayers except one or two obligatory prayers. Thus in 'Fawa'id' of 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami'. I said: whether after abundance or not, so a time-bound prayer is valid from one who left a month's prayer, then repented, and began performing time-bound prayers, then left an obligatory prayer. This is a branching of his statement: whether old or new, for when he began performing time-bound prayers, the missed prayers of the month become old, and they are abrogators of order. So if he leaves an obligatory prayer, it is permissible with his remembrance to perform a time-bound prayer after it.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the obligation of order (tartib) between missed prayers (fawa'it) and current time-bound prayers. The scenario: a person missed an entire month of prayers, then repented and began performing current prayers regularly. If after that he misses one current prayer while remembering the earlier missed month, his current prayer is still valid because the large number of missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it) has abrogated the requirement of order. The missed prayers are considered 'old' (qadima), meaning they are numerous enough to drop the order. The ruling is derived from the principle that necessity (i.e., preserving the current prayer's time) overrides strict sequencing. The author cites the 'Fawa'id' of al-Husami as source.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers (salat) that were not performed in their prescribed times.
قديمة (qadima): In this context, 'old' means that the missed prayers are numerous (generally considered more than 5 or 6) such that the order (tartib) between them and current prayers is abrogated.
مسقطة للترتيب (musqitat li al-tartib): Abrogators of order: the large number of missed prayers removes the obligation to perform them in sequence before current prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A large number of missed prayers (kathira) abrogates the obligation of order, so a current prayer remains valid even if the missed ones are remembered.

When Missed Prayers Become Few: Does Order Return?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on awd al-tartib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the return of order when missed prayers become few, and state the mufta bihi position with its proof.

Core Idea
Once order is dropped by abundance, it does not return when missed prayers become few.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person makes up all but one or two missed prayers, does the obligation to pray current prayers after making up the missed ones return? The majority of Hanafi authorities say no, analogizing to water purity, while a minority argue yes. Understanding this ruling has practical consequences for those with many missed prayers who gradually make them up.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the exact scenario: a person missed a month of prayers, then made up all except one or two. Now, while remembering these remaining missed prayers, he wishes to perform a current time-bound prayer.
2
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is whether the obligation of order (tartib) between missed prayers and current prayers returns when the number of missed prayers becomes small (qillat ba'd al-kathrah).
3
Analyze the majority Hanafi proof
The majority (al-Sarakhsi, author of al-Muhit, Qadi Khan) hold that order does not return. They analogize to impure water entering flowing abundant water: it becomes pure and does not revert to impurity when the water decreases. Similarly, once order is dropped due to abundance, it does not return.
This analogy is a qiyas that supports the permanence of the ruling.
4
Consider the minority view
Some mashayikh argue that order returns because the cause for dropping order (abundance) is no longer present. They implicitly rely on the principle that rulings follow their causes.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Muhit chose the majority view, and fatwa is upon it. The reasoning is that a ruling that has fallen (saqit) does not return automatically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو قضى صلاة الشهر إلا فرضاً أو فرضين. عبر عنها بلفظ: قيل، ومنهم من قال: مراده أنّ السنّة وما دونها إذا صارت فاصلة بينك وبين الفائتة، فالفائتة حديثة، وإذا فصل فوق الستة، فالفائتة قديمة. قوله: قلت بعد الكثرة أو لا، فإنَّه لما قضى صلاة الشهر إلا فرضاً أو فرضين قلت الفوائتُ بعد الكثرة، فلا يعودُ التَّرتيبُ الأَوَّل إلا أن يقضي الكُلِّ، وعند بعض المشايخ إن قلت بعد الكثرة يعودُ التّرتيب، واختار الإمامُ السِّرَخْسِي الأول، قال صاحبُ «المحيط»: وعليه الفتوى. صلى خمساً ذاكراً فائتة فسد الخمس موقوفاً. ومال إلى الجواز أبو حفص الكبير، واختاره من المشايخ فخر الإسلام وشمس الأئمة، وصاحب «المحيط»، وقاضي خان وغيرهم، ووجهه أن الترتيب لَمَّا سقط، فالساقط لا يعود كماء نجس دخل الماء الجاري، حتى كثر وسال، ثم عاد إلى القلّة، لا يصير نجساً.

He expressed it with the word 'said', and some of them said: his meaning is that the supererogatory and what is below it, when it becomes a separator between you and the missed prayer, then the missed prayer is new, and when it separates above six, then the missed prayer is old. Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the obligation of order (tartib) returns when the number of missed prayers becomes small after having been large. The scenario: a person missed a month of prayers, then made up all except one or two. Now, while remembering these remaining missed prayers, he performs a current time-bound prayer. The majority of early Hanafi authorities (including Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Muhit) hold that the order does not return, so the current prayer is valid. A minority (some mashayikh) say the order returns when the missed prayers become few, invalidating the current prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that order does not return, analogizing it to impure water that, when mixed with large flowing water, becomes pure and does not revert to impurity when the flowing water decreases. The passage also mentions the ruling that if one prays five prayers while remembering one missed prayer, all five are invalid (fasid mawqufan) pending the makeup of the missed one, but Abu Hafs al-Kabir and others argue for validity based on the principle that what has fallen does not return.

Key Terms
قلت بعد الكثرة (qillat ba'd al-kathrah): The state where missed prayers become few (e.g., one or two) after having been many (e.g., a month).
عود الترتيب (awd al-tartib): Return of the obligation to perform missed prayers in order before current prayers.
فساد موقوف (fasad mawquf): Conditional invalidity: the prayer is invalid only if the missed prayer is not made up later; if made up, the current prayer becomes valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Zuhr prayer is invalid because order returns when missed prayers become few.
B) The Zuhr prayer is valid because order does not return.
C) The Zuhr prayer is valid only if he also makes up the two after.
D) The Zuhr prayer is makruh and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when missed prayers become few after being many, the obligation of order does not return; the current prayer remains valid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Suspended Invalidity of Five Prayers
Intra-Hanafi dispute on suspended invalidity of five prayers after a missed one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's suspended invalidity and the Sahibayn's immediate invalidity, and apply the mufta bihi position to a scenario.

Core Idea
Five prayers after a missed one are invalid in a suspended sense; a sixth prayer can restore validity.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if someone remembers a missed obligatory prayer and then prays five on-time prayers, what is the status of those five? The answer divides the Hanafi school between immediate invalidity (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and suspended invalidity (Abu Hanifa). Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi concept of tartib (order) and how it interacts with the category of mawquf rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
A person misses one prayer (any obligatory prayer, even witr). While remembering that missed prayer, he prays five subsequent on-time prayers. What is the ruling on those five?
The missed prayer could be, e.g., Fajr; the five could be Zuhr, 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha, and the next Fajr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that the five prayers are invalid in a suspended (mawquf) manner. Their final status depends on a future action: if a sixth prayer is performed (or the time of the fifth exits), the five become valid; if the missed prayer is made up first, they become nafl.
Suspended invalidity is a unique Hanafi concept; the prayers are not immediately and definitively invalid.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the five prayers are invalid immediately and definitively (fasād bātt). They argue that the order (tartīb) is still obligatory, and the abundance that abrogates order only counts if it occurs before any prayer is performed.
This is based on qiyas: the rule for abrogation of order by abundance is conditional on abundance existing before starting to pray.
4
Understand the usul basis
Sahibayn rely on strict analogy (qiyas): the abrogating abundance must be present before any prayer. Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: the order can be abrogated once the total missed prayers reach six, so suspension allows for that possibility. The analogy of impure water becoming pure when abundant pure water flows in is cited.
This difference in usul (qiyas vs istihsan) is typical in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's. Therefore, if someone prays five prayers after missing one, they should not immediately repeat them. If they then pray a sixth (or the time of the fifth exits), the five become valid as obligatory prayers. If they instead make up the missed prayer first, the five become nafl and must be repeated as farḍ.
Most later Hanafi authorities, like al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Muhit, affirmed Abu Hanifa's view.
