Disputes on Sajdah al-Sahw: Criterion and Jahr/Sirr
Intra-Hanafi commentary on Sajdah al-Sahw with two sub-disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three intra-Hanafi disputes on Sajdah al-Sahw (criterion, jahr/sirr for munfarid, amount of delay) and apply the mufta bihi position to each.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Sahw compensates for omitting a wajib; its obligation depends on the nature and extent of the omission.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a detailed intra-Hanafi analysis of Sajdah al-Sahw causes. The commentator clarifies disagreements on the criterion for delay, the effect of loud/quiet recitation changes, and the minimum amount of delay that triggers obligation. Understanding these ikhtilafat is crucial for correctly applying the rulings in prayer. We will walk through each dispute, identify the competing views, and determine the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three points of contention
The passage discusses three separate issues: (a) the criterion for delay that obligates Sajdah al-Sahw (amount of a rukn vs. specific wording like 'wa 'ala ali Muhammad'), (b) whether a change in jahr/sirr recitation obligates Sajdah al-Sahw for a munfarid (individual worshipper), and (c) the amount of delay (any amount vs. a rukn's worth).
These are intra-Hanafi differences, not cross-madhhab.
2
Compare the competing views and their evidence
For each dispute, note the two positions and the scholars who hold them. For jahr/sirr, the hadith of the Prophet occasionally reciting audibly in silent prayers is cited as evidence that occasional change does not by itself obligate Sajdah al-Sahw.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim (thubut zanni, dalala zanni).
3
Apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi
The commentator gives preference: for the criterion, Ghazzi's view (a rukn); for jahr in sirr, the view of Bada'i' and others (obligates for both imam and munfarid); for sirr in jahr, the view of Zayla'i and Hidayah (only imam) is the apparent transmission; for amount, the view of Ibn al-Humam et al. (a rukn's worth).
The tarjih is based on later scholars' corrections and the general principle of reverting to leaving a wajib.
4
Relate all causes to the principle of leaving a wajib
The commentator summarizes that all causes of Sajdah al-Sahw ultimately involve the omission of a wajib (obligatory element), whether by adding, omitting, or altering recitation or order. This principle unifies the various triggers.
This principle is attributed to Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and approved by the author of al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وركوعين، والجهر وقيل : لا يجب سجود السهو بقوله : اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ على محمد، ونحوه، وإنما المعتبر مقدار ما يؤدي فيه رُكْناً، وركوعين ، والجهرُ [؟] في القول بوجوبه بالتأخير قدر أداء ركن كما اختاره الغَزّي في تنوير الأبصار، وقيل : لا يجب ما لم يقل : وعلى آل محمّد، قال الحلبي في «شرح المنية الصغير»: هو الأصح، وهو قول الأكثر. [١] قوله : وإنّما المعتبر؛ ظاهره تغاير القولين، والحق أن ما لهما واحد، إلا أن يراد بمقدار أداء ركن ما زاد عليه. [٢]قوله : والجهر ؛ أي الجهر بالقراءة في صلاة يخافتُ فيها ؛ أي يجب عليه أن يقرأ سراً، وكذا عكسه؛ أي السرّ في الصلاة الجهرية، وهذا في حق الإمام دون المنفرد ، بناءً على أن وجوب السرّ والجهر من خصائص الجماعة، على ما اختاره الزَّيْلَعي، وصاحب «الهداية». لكن الذي صححه صاحب «البدائع»، و«الدرر»، ومال إليه في «الفتح» و«البحر»، و«النهر»، و«الحلبة» وغيرها : أن وجوب سجود السهو بالجهر في السرية على كل مصلّ إماماً كان أو منفرداً، وفي عكسه على الإمام دون المنفرد. فالحاصل أن الجهر في الجهريَّة لا يجب على المنفرد اتفاقاً، واختلف في وجوب السر عليه ، وظاهر الرواية عدم الوجوب، واختلف في المقدار، فظاهر الرواية وجوب سجود السهو بالجهر في السريّة مطلقاً، وكذا عكسه ولو بقدر كلمة، والذي صححه ابن الهمام والزيلعي وصاحب «الهداية» : إنّ الوجوب في قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة في الصورتين لا أقل منه ، فقد ثبت عن النبي ﷺ أنه كان يُسر في سرية، ويسمعهم الآية أحياناً، أخرجه الشيخان. [١] قوله : يخافت ؛ معروف أو مجهول من المخافتة. [٢]قوله : الأول ؛ احتراز عن الأخير ؛ لكونه فرضاً عندنا كما مر في موضعه، فلا يجب بتركه سجود السهو. [٣] قوله : وقيل ؛ قائله صدر الإسلام أبو اليسر البزدوي، أخو فخر الإسلام، واستحسنه صاحب «المحيط». [٤]قوله : كل هذه ؛ أي كلّ ما ذُكِرَ من موجباتِ سجدة السهو يرجع إلى تركِ الواجب، فإنَّ الجهر في موضع السرّ يستلزم ترك السرّ، والسر ترك الجهر، وتقديم الركن فيه ترك لواجب الترتيب، وكذا تأخيره فيه ترك الوصل الواجب، وكذا في تكرار الركن.
And two bowings, and the loudness. And it was said: Sajdah al-Sahw is not required by saying 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad' and the like; rather the criterion is the amount in which one performs a pillar. And two bowings, and the loudness [unclear] regarding the view of its obligation due to delay by the amount of performing a pillar, as chosen by al-Ghazzi in Tanwir al-Absar. And it was said: It is not required unless one says 'and upon the family of Muhammad.' Al-Halabi said in Sharh al-Munyah al-Saghir: It is the most correct, and it is the view of the majority. [1] His saying: 'Rather the criterion' - apparently the two views differ, but the truth is that they are one, unless by 'amount of performing a pillar' is meant something more. [2] His saying: 'And the loudness' - i.e., loud recitation in a prayer in which one is silent; i.e., he must recite silently, and likewise its opposite, i.e., silence in a loud prayer. This applies to the imam, not the individual, based on the view that the obligation of silence and loudness is a characteristic of the congregation, according to what al-Zayla'i and the author of al-Hidayah chose. But what the author of al-Bada'i', al-Durar, and those inclined in al-Fath, al-Bahr, al-Nahr, al-Halabah and others have corrected is that the obligation of Sajdah al-Sahw due to loudness in a silent prayer applies to every worshipper, whether imam or individual, and in its opposite it applies to the imam only, not the individual. So the conclusion is that loudness in a loud prayer is not obligatory for the individual by agreement, and they differed on the obligation of silence upon him. The apparent transmission is the non-obligation. They differed on the amount. The apparent transmission is the obligation of Sajdah al-Sahw due to loudness in a silent prayer absolutely, and likewise its opposite even if by a word. And what Ibn al-Humam, al-Zayla'i, and the author of al-Hidayah have corrected is that the obligation is in the amount that makes the prayer valid in both cases, not less than that. For it has been established from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he used to be silent in a silent prayer, and make them hear the verse occasionally, recorded by al-Bukhari and Muslim. [1] His saying: 'he is silent' - either known or passive from silence. [2] His saying: 'the first' - a precaution for the last, because it is fard according to us as previously mentioned in its place, so Sajdah al-Sahw is not required for leaving it. [3] His saying: 'and it was said' - its speaker is Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, brother of Fakhr al-Islam, and the author of al-Muhit deemed it good. [4] His saying: 'all these' - i.e., all that has been mentioned of the causes of Sajdah al-Sahw revert to leaving an obligatory element. For loudness in the place of silence necessitates leaving silence, and silence in place of loudness necessitates leaving loudness. And advancing a pillar therein involves leaving the obligatory order, and likewise delaying it involves leaving the obligatory connection, and likewise in repeating the pillar.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute commentary on the causes of Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in prayer. The commentator first addresses the criterion for when Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib due to delay. Two opinions are presented: the first (chosen by al-Ghazzi) holds that it is obligated if the delay amounts to the time taken to perform one rukn (pillar); the second (considered more correct by al-Halabi and the majority) requires that the delayed phrase include the mention of the Prophet's family (آل محمد). The commentator reconciles these views, noting that the true difference is negligible unless 'amount of a rukn' implies extra time. Next, the ruling on loud and silent recitation as causes for Sajdah al-Sahw is detailed. Two positions are cited: al-Zayla'i and the author of al-Hidayah restrict the obligation to the imam only, while the authors of al-Bada'i', al-Durar, and others extend it to both imam and munfarid (individual) for loudness in a silent prayer, and for the opposite (silence in a loud prayer) only the imam is obligated. The upshot is agreement that loudness in a loud prayer does not obligate Sajdah al-Sahw for the munfarid; the point of contention is silence in a loud prayer for him. The apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) is that Sajdah al-Sahw is not required for the munfarid in that case. Regarding the amount of delay, the apparent transmission obligates Sajdah al-Sahw for even a single word, but Ibn al-Humam, al-Zayla'i, and the author of al-Hidayah restrict it to the amount that renders the prayer invalid (i.e., the minimum for a rukn). The prophetic hadith (from Abu Qatada) is cited as evidence: the Prophet would sometimes recite a verse audibly in silent prayers, indicating that occasional audible recitation does not break prayer but does not obligate Sajdah al-Sahw by itself. Finally, the commentator summarizes a general principle (attributed to Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and approved by the author of al-Muhit): all causes of Sajdah al-Sahw ultimately involve the omission of a wajib (obligatory element). Examples given: loudness in place of silence omits the wajib of silence; silence in place of loudness omits the wajib of loudness; advancing or delaying a pillar omits the wajib of proper order (tartib) or connection (wasl). Thus, Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib whenever any wajib is missed, whether by addition, omission, or alteration.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omissions or additions in prayer, whether they involve omitting a wajib or adding an extra action.
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, typically required in Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha for the imam.
السر (al-sirr): Silent recitation, required in Zuhr and Asr for the imam.
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligatory element that is less than fard; omission requires compensation (Sajdah al-Sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon position regarding Sajdah al-Sahw for a munfarid who recites audibly in a silent prayer like Zuhr?
A) Sajdah al-Sahw is required on both imam and munfarid for jahr in sirriyah.
B) Sajdah al-Sahw is required only on the imam; the munfarid does not do it.
C) Sajdah al-Sahw is not required for jahr in sirriyah at all.
D) Sajdah al-Sahw is required only if the munfarid recites more than one verse audibly.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib when a wajib is omitted; the precise triggers and amounts differ among Hanafi scholars, but the mufta bihi is clear for each sub-issue.

All Causes of Sujud al-Sahw Revert to Omitting a Wajib
States that all causes of prostration of forgetfulness ultimately revert to omitting a wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that all causes of sujud al-sahw revert to omitting a wajib and identify examples of wajib omissions in prayer.

Core Idea
Every cause of sujud al-sahw is ultimately an omission of a wajib.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi principle: the prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) is not for every mistake but specifically for omitting a wajib element in prayer. The matn and commentary explain that actions like reciting loudly where silence is required, or leaving the first sitting, all reduce to leaving a wajib. This insight helps you distinguish between fard, wajib, and sunnah in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific acts listed in the matn as causes of sujud al-sahw
Read the matn and note the examples: loud recitation where silent (and vice versa), and leaving the first sitting.
These are the concrete cases from which the principle is derived.
2
Understand the commentary's explanation: each act reduces to omitting a wajib
The commentary shows that loudness in a silent place entails omitting the wajib of silence, and so on. Observe how the commentator traces each example back to leaving a wajib.
The key is that the wajib is an act that must be done in a specific manner; altering it is a form of omission.
3
Recognize the difference of opinion (qila) and the preferred view
The matn uses 'qila' (it is said) indicating some scholars hold that not all causes are reducible. The commentary then endorses the view that all causes revert to wajib, citing al-Bazdawi and the authors of al-Kanz and al-Tabyin.
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the unifying factor is wajib omission.
4
Apply the principle to the final sitting
The commentary explicitly notes that leaving the final sitting (which is fard) does not require sujud al-sahw. This shows that the principle applies only to wajib, not fard.
If a fard is omitted, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, not compensated by sujud.
5
Appreciate the tarjih and authority behind the principle
The author of al-Tabyin is quoted as saying 'the correct view is that it becomes obligatory by omitting a wajib only.' This is the mufta bihi position.
This principle simplifies the rules of sujud al-sahw into a single criterion.

Source Text

فيما يخافت وعكسه، وترك القعود الأول ، وقيل : كل هذه يؤول إلى تركِ الواجب

[١] قوله : يخافت ؛ معروف أو مجهول من المخافتة. [٢]قوله : الأول ؛ احتراز عن الأخير ؛ لكونه فرضاً عندنا كما مر في موضعه، فلا يجب بتركه سجود السهو. [٣] قوله : وقيل ؛ قائله صدر الإسلام أبو اليسر البزدوي، أخو فخر الإسلام، واستحسنه صاحب «المحيط».

Book of Prayer: Prostration of Forgetfulness. Regarding that which is silently recited and its opposite, and leaving the first sitting, and it is said: all these revert to omitting a wajib. [1] His saying: 'yukhafit' – known or passive from mukhdafata. [2] His saying: 'al-awwal' – a precaution against the last, because it is a fard according to us as previously mentioned in its place, so sujud al-sahw is not obligatory for leaving it. [3] His saying: 'qila' – its proponent is Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, brother of Fakhr al-Islam, and it was deemed good by the author of al-Muhit. [4] His saying: 'all these' – i.e., all that has been mentioned of causes of the prostration of forgetfulness revert to omitting a wajib: loudness in a place of silence entails omitting silence, silence entails omitting loudness, advancing a pillar entails omitting the wajib of order, likewise delaying it entails omitting the wajib of connection, and likewise in repeating a pillar. (1) It is the choice of the author of al-Kanz, and it was corrected by the author of al-Tabyin, who said: the correct view is that it becomes obligatory by omitting a wajib only, and this is because in advancing, delaying, and changing there is omitting a wajib; because what is obligatory upon him is not to do thus, so when he does it he has omitted the wajib, so omitting the wajib encompasses everything.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn with commentary establishing the principle that all causes of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) ultimately come back to omitting a wajib. The matn lists examples: reciting loudly where one should be silent, silently where loud, and leaving the first sitting. The commentary elaborates: 'al-awwal' (first sitting) excludes the final sitting because that is fard, so leaving it does not require sujud. The view that all causes revert to omitting a wajib is attributed to Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi and is the choice of the author of al-Kanz and al-Tabyin. The commentary explains that actions like advancing or delaying a pillar entail omitting the wajib of order or connection, thus the wajib category covers all causes.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahwi): Prostration performed to compensate for unintentional errors (sahw) in prayer, such as omission of a wajib or performing an extra action.
القعود الأول (al-qu‘ūd al-awwal): The first sitting in a prayer of three or four rak‘ahs, between the first two rak‘ahs.
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligatory act in prayer that is less than fard; its omission requires compensation (sujud al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
All causes of sujud al-sahw ultimately stem from unintentionally omitting a wajib, not a fard or sunnah.

Threshold for Sujud al-Sahw in Loudness and Softness
Ruling on the threshold for sujud al-sahw regarding loudness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-sahw for loudness in silent prayer and identify the threshold that obligates sujud.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is required only when the change in loudness reaches an amount that would suffice for prayer, not for any deviation.

This passage addresses a common error: thinking that any loudness or softness in the wrong type of prayer requires sujud al-sahw. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes between trivial and significant deviations. Understanding the threshold (qadr ma tajuza bihi al-salah) is essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is loudness in a silent prayer (or softness in a loud prayer). The dispute is whether any amount triggers sujud or only a significant amount.
The issue is purely within the Hanafi school; both views are Hanafi.
2
State the early view
Some earlier Hanafis held that even a single word of loudness in a silent prayer (or vice versa) obligates sujud al-sahw.
This is based on a strict application of the rule that any change from the prescribed norm requires compensation.
3
State the corrected (mufta bihi) view
The corrected view, supported by Ibn al-Humam, al-Zayla‘i, and the author of al-Hidayah, is that sujud is wajib only when the deviation is in the amount that suffices for prayer (قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة).
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
4
Locate the proof
The proof is the hadith from Abu Qatada that the Prophet would occasionally recite a verse audibly in silent prayers. This shows that a small amount of change does not necessitate sujud.
The hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone recites a short phrase (less than the minimal sufficing amount) audibly in a silent prayer, the early view requires sujud, but the mufta bihi view does not.
The threshold is generally one verse of at least six letters.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The prostration of forgetfulness [is required] for loudness in silent prayer absolutely, and likewise its opposite, even if by [as little as] the extent of a word. What Ibn al-Humam, al-Zayla‘i, and the author of al-Hidayah corrected is that the obligation is in the amount that suffices for prayer in both cases, not less than that. For it has been established from the Prophet that he would recite softly in his silent prayers and make them hear the verse occasionally, related by al-Bukhari and Muslim. Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sujud al-sahw for loudness in silent prayers and vice versa. The matn states that sujud is required for loudness in a silent prayer absolutely, and likewise for silence in a loud prayer, even if only to the extent of a word. However, the corrected view of Ibn al-Humam, al-Zayla‘i, and the author of al-Hidayah is that obligation arises only when the change is in an amount that would be sufficient for the prayer (قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة), which is the minimal recitation that validates the prayer (e.g., one verse of at least six letters). The proof is the hadith from Abu Qatada that the Prophet would occasionally make the congregation hear a verse in a silent prayer, indicating that a small amount of loudness does not necessarily require sujud. So the relied-upon position is that if the loudness or softness is less than the minimal amount that suffices, sujud is not obligatory; if it is equal to or more, sujud is required.

Key Terms
الجهر في السريّة (al-jahr fī al-sirriyyah): Reciting loudly in a prayer where silent recitation is prescribed (e.g., Zuhr, Asr).
قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة (qadr mā tajūzu bihi al-ṣalāh): The minimal amount of recitation that makes the prayer valid, which is generally considered to be one verse of at least six letters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw for loudness in silent prayer is wajib only when the deviation is in the amount that suffices for prayer.

Follower's Forgetfulness and Returning to First Sitting
Rulings on follower's forgetfulness and return to first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings on the follower's forgetfulness and the forgetting of the first sitting, and apply the condition of proximity to determine when to return and when to perform sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
The follower has no independent sujud al-sahw; he follows the imam. For forgetting the first sitting, return if closer to sitting.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the legal status of forgetfulness in congregational prayer. It addresses three key situations: when the follower forgets, when the imam forgets, and when someone forgets the first sitting. The rulings hinge on the principle of complete following of the imam and the proximity to the sitting position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and list the three distinct rulings: (1) follower's forgetfulness does not obligate sujud, (2) the masbuq prostrates with the imam and then completes his prayer, (3) forgetting the first sitting: return and no sujud if closer to sitting, otherwise do not return and perform sujud.
The rulings are stated in the first paragraph and then explained.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed' is cited as the basis for the first two rulings. Understand how it implies that the follower's forgetfulness does not create an obligation because he is a follower.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud, Bukhari, and Muslim.
3
Analyze the condition for returning
The text specifies that returning to the first sitting depends on proximity. Determine what 'closer to sitting' means: the first half of standing is not yet completed. If equal, count as closer to standing.
Refer to al-Kafi for the exact definition.
4
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Practice: If a follower forgets and performs sujud, is it valid? (No, he should not; he should follow the imam). If the imam forgets and does not prostrate, does the follower? (No). If a person forgets the first sitting and is halfway up, what should he do? (Do not return, perform sujud).
These applications test understanding.

۲۷۰
عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
ولا يجب بسهو المؤتم، بل يجب بسهو إمامه إن سجد، والمسبوق يسجد مع إمامه ، ثم يقضي ما فات عنه ، ومَن سَها عن القعدة الأولى، وهو إليها أقرب عاد ولا
سهو
[١] قوله : ولا يجب ؛ أي لا يجب سجود السهو بسهو المقتدي لا على الإمام ؛ لأنه تبع، والتبع لا يوجب شيئاً على الأصل، ولا عليه ؛ لأنه لا يمكن له أداؤه لا قبل السلام للزومِ مخالفة الإمام ، ولا بعده لخروجه عن الصلاة بسلام الإمام، وكذا لا يجب عليه إن سها إمامه ولم يسجد ، والأصلُ في ذلك كله حديث : «إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به»(۳)، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره الدال على وجوب المتابعة.
[٢]قوله : يسجد مع إمامه ؛ سواء كان السهو من الإمام قبل اقتدائه أو بعده ، وفيه إشارة إلى أنّه لا يتابع الإمام في السلام ؛ لئلا يقع في خلال صلاته ، بل يسجد معه ويتشهد ، فإذا سلّم الإمامُ بعد سجدة السهو قام إلى قضاء ما فاته. [٣]قوله : وهو ؛ أي والحال أنّ المصلّي إلى القعدة أقرب، بأن لم يكن النصفُ
الأوّل مستوياً، فإن استوى عدّ قرب القيام. كذا في «الكافي».
[٤]قوله : عاد ؛ لأنّ ما يقرب من الشيء يأخذ حكمه ، فصار كأنه لم يقم. 01 ] قوله : ولا سهو ؛ هذا هو الأصح. كما في «الهداية»(4).
(1) أما لو سقط عن الإمام بسبب من الأسباب بأن تكلم أو أحدث متعمداً أو خرج من المسجد، فإنه يسقط عن المقتدي، ينظر: البحر» (۱) (۱۰۷) قال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار) (١ : ٤٩٨) : والظاهر أن المقتدي تجب عليه الإعادة كالإمام إن كان السقوط بفعله العمد ؛ لتقرر النقصان بلا جابر من غير عذر.

٣٠٩)، وغيرها.
(٤) «الهداية» (١ : ٥٠٨).
270. ‘Umdat al-Ri‘ayah ‘ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. And it is not obligatory due to the follower’s forgetfulness, but it is obligatory due to his imam’s forgetfulness if he prostrates. And the one who is preceded (masbuq) prostrates with his imam, then makes up what he missed. And whoever forgets the first sitting, while he is closer to it, he returns and there is no sujud. [1] His saying: 'and it is not obligatory' – i.e., sujud al-sahw is not obligatory due to the follower’s forgetfulness, neither upon the imam because he is a follower, and the follower does not obligate anything upon the leader, nor upon himself because he cannot perform it: not before the salaam due to necessitating opposing the imam, nor after due to exiting the prayer by the imam’s salaam. Similarly, it is not obligatory for him if his imam forgets and does not prostrate. The basis for all this is the hadith: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed' reported by Abu Dawud and others, indicating the obligation of following. [2] His saying: 'prostrates with his imam' – whether the forgetfulness occurred before his joining or after. There is an indication that he does not follow the imam in the salaam, lest he fall in the middle of his prayer; rather he prostrates with him and recites tashahhud. When the imam makes salaam after the sujud, he stands to make up what he missed. [3] His saying: 'he is closer' – i.e., while the prayer is closer to the sitting, such that the first half is not equal; if it is equal, the proximity to standing is considered. This is in al-Kafi. [4] His saying: 'he returns' – because what is close to a thing takes its ruling, so it is as if he did not stand. [5] His saying: 'and no sujud' – this is the most correct, as in al-Hidayah. (1) But if it falls from the imam for some reason, such as if he speaks or intentionally breaks wudu or leaves the mosque, then it falls from the follower. See al-Bahr. Ibn ‘Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar said: apparently, the follower must repeat like the imam if the fall was due to his intentional action, because the deficiency is settled without a compensator without excuse. (2) But if he returns while he is closer to standing, he prostrates for sujud. See Nur al-Idah. (3) Sunan Abi Dawud (1:221), Sahih al-Bukhari (1:253), Sahih Muslim (1:309), etc. (4) Al-Hidayah (1:508).
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage contains three rulings with their evidence. First: the follower’s (muqtadi) forgetfulness does not obligate sujud al-sahw, neither upon the imam (as follower does not bind imam) nor upon the follower himself (as he cannot perform it without breaking prayer). The proof is the hadith 'the imam is appointed to be followed', which obligates following the imam completely. If the imam forgets and does not prostrate, the follower also does not prostrate. Second: the one who joined late (masbuq) prostrates with his imam, then after the imam’s salam he stands to complete his missed rak‘ahs. He does not follow the imam in the salam because his prayer is still ongoing. Third: if someone forgets the first sitting (al-qa‘dah al-ula) and is closer to sitting (i.e., his rising is not yet dominant, or the first half of standing is not yet reached), he should return to the sitting and does not need to perform sujud. But if he is closer to standing (e.g., has already stood up more than halfway), he should not return and must perform sujud al-sahw. The basis is that closeness to an action gives it the same ruling.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower in congregational prayer (muqtadi).
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who joins the congregation late after missing one or more rak‘ahs.
القعود الأولى (al-qu‘ūd al-ūlā): The first sitting in a three or four rak‘ah prayer, between the first two rak‘ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He should prostrate with the imam and then stand to complete his missed rak‘ahs
C) He should prostrate alone after the imam finishes
D) He should repeat the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
In congregational prayer, the follower has no independent sujud al-sahw; he follows the imam. For forgetting the first sitting, return if closer to sitting, else perform sujud.

intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Sajdah al-Sahw for the Follower and Preceded
States that sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory on the follower but follows the imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-sahw for the follower and the masbuq, explain the proof from the hadith, and identify the practical consequences for prayer.

Core Idea
The follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; he follows the imam's sajdah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains a key Hanafi rule about sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) specifically for the person praying behind an imam (mu'tam) and the person who joins late (masbuq). The central principle is that the follower is a dependent (tabi') and does not initiate any independent action, including sajdah al-sahw. The ruling is derived from the famous hadith that the imam was only appointed to be followed. We will walk through the ruling, the evidence, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on sajdah al-sahw for the follower's own forgetfulness? Is it obligatory?
The text states it is not obligatory (la yajib).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite?
The hadith: 'The imam was only appointed to be followed.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove that the follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw?
The phrase 'li-yu'tamma bihi' (to be followed) indicates that the follower must not act independently.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any other school disagree?
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the follower must perform sajdah for his own forgetfulness.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon in the Hanafi school?
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, based on the principle of following.

ولا يجب بسهو المؤتم، بل يجب بسهو إمامه إن سجد، والمسبوق يسجد مع إمامه، ثم يقضي ما فات عنه.
[١] قوله : ولا يجب؛ أي لا يجب سجود السهو بسهو المقتدي لا على الإمام؛ لأنه تبع، والتبع لا يوجب شيئاً على الأصل، ولا عليه؛ لأنه لا يمكن له أداؤه لا قبل السلام للزومِ مخالفة الإمام، ولا بعده لخروجه عن الصلاة بسلام الإمام، وكذا لا يجب عليه إن سها إمامه ولم يسجد، والأصلُ في ذلك كله حديث: «إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به»(۳)، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره الدال على وجوب المتابعة.

(١) أما لو سقط عن الإمام بسبب من الأسباب بأن تكلم أو أحدث متعمداً أو خرج من المسجد، فإنه يسقط عن المقتدي، ينظر: البحر» (۱) (۱۰۷) قال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار) (١ : ٤٩٨) : والظاهر أن المقتدي تجب عليه الإعادة كالإمام إن كان السقوط بفعله العمد؛ لتقرر النقصان بلا جابر من غير عذر.

And it is not obligatory due to the forgetfulness of the follower, rather it is obligatory due to the forgetfulness of his imam if he prostrates, and the preceded one prostrates with his imam, then he makes up what he missed. [1] His statement: 'And it is not obligatory': meaning, sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory due to the forgetfulness of the follower, neither upon the imam because he is a follower, and a follower does not impose anything upon the original, nor upon himself because he cannot perform it, neither before the salam due to necessary opposition to the imam, nor after it due to his exit from prayer by the imam's salam. Likewise, it is not obligatory upon him if his imam forgets and does not prostrate. The basis for all this is the hadith: 'The imam was only appointed to be followed' - narrated by Abu Dawud and others, indicating the obligation of following. [2] His statement: 'He prostrates with his imam' - whether the forgetfulness of the imam was before his following or after. And in it is an indication that he does not follow the imam in the salam, lest he be in the middle of his prayer. Rather, he prostrates with him and recites the tashahhud, and when the imam makes salam after the prostration of forgetfulness, he stands to make up what he missed. (1) As for if it is nullified for the imam due to some reason, such as he spoke or intentionally performed an invalidating act or left the mosque, then it is nullified for the follower; see: al-Bahr (1:107). Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar (1:498): Apparently, the follower must repeat the prayer like the imam if the nullification was due to his intentional action, because the deficiency was established without a remedy without excuse. (3) In Sunan Abi Dawud (1): 221, and Sahih al-Bukhari (1): 253, and Sahih Muslim (1): 309, and others.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) for the mu'tam (follower) and the masbuq (the one who joined late). The key principle: the follower is not obligated to perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness because he is a follower (tabi'), and a follower does not create obligation for the one followed (the imam). Additionally, the follower himself cannot perform sajdah al-sahw independently: not before the imam's salam (as that would violate following the imam) and not after (since his prayer ends with the imam's salam - however, note that later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Abidin discuss if the imam's prayer is invalidated before salam). The proof is the hadith 'innama ju'ila al-imamu li-yu'tamma bihi' (The imam was only appointed to be followed) which establishes the obligation of following the imam in all actions. The masbuq (one who joined late) must prostrate with the imam if the imam performs sajdah al-sahw, whether the imam's forgetfulness occurred before or after the masbuq joined. Importantly, the masbuq does not follow the imam in salam; rather, he prostrates with the imam, recites tashahhud, and after the imam's salam, he stands to complete his missed rak'ahs. The footnote adds that if the imam's need for sajdah is nullified (e.g., due to intentional speech or leaving the mosque), it is also nullified for the follower, but if the imam's lapse was deliberate, the follower may need to repeat the prayer.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The person praying behind an imam (follower).
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and has missed some rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower forgets to recite a wajib (e.g., al-Fatihah) but the imam does not forget, must the follower perform sajdah al-sahw?
A) Yes, because he is responsible for his own prayer.
B) No, because the follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw independently; he only follows the imam.
C) Yes, but only if it was a fard act.
D) No, sajdah al-sahw is never required for the follower.

Key Takeaway
The follower is not required to perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; he follows the imam's sajdah if performed.

Forgetting the First and Last Tashahhud: When to Return, When to Continue
Commentary on rulings for forgetfulness in the first and last sittings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for forgetting the first and last tashahhud sittings, distinguishing between cases based on proximity to standing or prostrating, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute about returning when closer to standing.

Core Idea
The first sitting is a wajib; the last is a fard – each has distinct rules for returning and sajdah al-sahw.

Forgetfulness in the prayer sittings is common, but the Hanafi school provides precise guidelines. This lesson unpacks the rules for the first (wajib) and last (fard) sittings, the critical role of physical posture (closer to sitting or standing), and the point of no return after committing to the next prostration. We will also examine a hadith proof and a key dispute among later Hanafis.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two sittings
The first sitting (after two rak'ahs in 3 or 4 rak'ah prayers) is a wajib; the last sitting is a fard. This difference affects the rules for returning when forgotten.
Recall: wajib omission requires sajdah al-sahw; fard omission may invalidate if not corrected before the next rukn.
2
Apply the rule for first sitting
If the praying person forgets the first sitting and is physically closer to sitting (not fully stood), he returns and no sajdah is needed. If closer to standing (or equal), he continues and performs sajdah al-sahw at the end.
The measure: if the first half of the body is not yet upright, he is considered closer to sitting.
3
Apply the rule for last sitting
If the last sitting is forgotten, he must return to it as long as he has not yet performed the prostration (sajdah) of the next rak'ah. Once he has prostrated (even one sajdah), he cannot return and must perform sajdah al-sahw.
This is called 'al-taqyid bi al-sajdah' – committing to the prostration.
4
Recognize the proof from hadith
The hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah (recorded in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar) directly supports these rulings: if one rises and has not fully stood, he sits back; if fully stood, he continues and does sajdah al-sahw.
The hadith uses 'if he does not complete the standing' – interpreted as not yet having fully risen.
5
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
If a person returns to the first sitting when he should have continued (i.e., when closer to standing), does the prayer become invalid? The mashhur view says yes (abandoning the wajib standing), but Ibn al-Humam preferred non-invalidity, as the addition is less than a rak'ah.
The mufta bihi later is non-invalidity, as per Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[٤] قوله : عاد؛ لأنّ ما يقرب من الشيء يأخذ حكمه، فصار كأنه لم يقم.
[٥] قوله : ولا سهو؛ هذا هو الأصح. كما في «الهداية»(4).
(٢) أما إذا عاد وهو إلى القيام أقرب سجد للسهو. ينظر : «نور الإيضاح»(ص٢٢٥).

[٢] قوله : وسجد للسهو؛ أي من غير فرق بين أن يكون إلى القعود أقرب أو إلى القيام، فإنّ القرب من القعود وإن جاز أن يعطى له حكم القاعد إلا أنه ليس بقاعد حقيقة، فاعتبر جانب الحقيقة فيما إذا سها عن الأخيرة، وحكم القاعد في السهو عن الأولى إظهاراً للتفاوتِ بين الفرض والواجب. كذا في «النهر»
[٣] قوله : وإن قيد؛ أي إن سجدَ للركعة الثالثة في الثنائية، والخامسة في الرباعية، والرابعة في الثلاثية.
(١) فعن قيس بن أبي حازم قال: «صلى بنا المغيرة بن شعبة فقام من الركعتين قائماً، فقلنا: سبحان الله فأومى، وقال: سبحان الله، فمضى في صلاته فلما قضى صلاته وسَلَّمَ سجد سجدتين، وهو جالس، ثم قال: صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاستوى قائماً من جلوسه فمضى في صلاته فلما قضى صلاته سجد سجدتين وهو جالس، ثم قال: إذا صلى أحدكم فقام من الجلوس فإن لم يستتم فليجلس وليس عليه سجدتان، فإن استوى قائماً فليمض في صلاته، وليسجد سجدتين وهو جالس» في شرح معاني الآثار (1:440)، وسنده صحيح كما في «إعلاء السنن» (16:169)، وغيره.
(٢) في «فتح القدير» (509)، وقال: «ذا وفي النفس من التصحيح شيء وذلك لأن غاية الأمر في الرجوع إلى القعدة الأولى أن يكون زيادة قيام ما في الصلاة وهو وإن كان لا يحل لكنه بالصحة لا يحل لما عرف أن زيادة ما دون الركعة لا تفسد إلا أن يفرق باقتران هذه الزيادة بالرفض، لكن قد يقال المتحقق لزوم الإثم أيضا بالرفض، أما الفساد فلم يظهـر وجـه استلزامه إياه فيترجح بهذا البحث القول المقابل للمصحح»

And whoever forgets the first sitting, and he is closer to it, he returns and there is no sajdah. [3] His statement: 'and he is': meaning, while the praying person is closer to the sitting, such that the first half is not equal; if it is equal, then he is considered closer to standing. Thus in al-Kafi. [4] His statement: 'he returns': because that which is close to something takes its ruling, so it is as if he did not stand. [5] His statement: 'and there is no sajdah': this is the most correct. As in al-Hidayah (4). (2) As for if he returns while he is closer to standing, he prostrates for forgetfulness. See: Nur al-Idah (p.225). (4) al-Hidayah (1:508). Otherwise he stands and prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he forgets the last sitting, he returns as long as he has not committed to the prostration, and prostrates for forgetfulness; and if he has committed, [he does not return]. [1] His statement: 'Otherwise': meaning, if he is not closer to sitting, he stands and abandons the sitting, and prostrates for forgetfulness at the end of his prayer. This is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, as recorded by the authors of the Sunan. And does his prayer become invalid if he returns in this situation? The well-known view among our companions is that it is invalid due to necessitating abandoning the obligatory (the standing for the wajib), but Ibn al-Humam preferred the view of non-invalidity. [2] His statement: 'and prostrates for forgetfulness': meaning, without distinction between being closer to sitting or to standing, because closeness to sitting, although it may give him the ruling of one sitting, he is not actually sitting, so the aspect of reality is considered when he forgets the last sitting, and the ruling of the sitter in forgetfulness of the first is to show the difference between the fard and the wajib. Thus in al-Nahr. [3] His statement: 'and if he has committed': meaning, if he has prostrated for the third rak'ah in a two-rak'ah prayer, or the fifth in a four-rak'ah prayer, or the fourth in a three-rak'ah prayer. (1) From Qays ibn Abi Hazim: 'Mughirah ibn Shu'bah led us in prayer and stood from the two rak'ahs standing...' (full hadith). (2) In Fath al-Qadir (509): '... there is something in the heart regarding this correction...' (3) See: al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (1:328).
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings when one forgets the first sitting (qa'dah ula) or the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in prayer. For the first sitting, if the praying person is physically closer to sitting (i.e., has not fully risen to standing, typically measured by whether the first half of the body is upright), he should return to sitting and no sajdah al-sahw is required. The principle: that which is close to something takes its ruling – since he hasn't fully stood, it is as if he never stood. However, if he is closer to standing (or equal), he must continue standing and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end. For the last sitting (which is a fard, not wajib), if he forgets it and rises, he must return to sitting as long as he has not yet performed the sajdah of the subsequent rak'ah (i.e., 'committed' to the next rak'ah by prostrating). If he has prostrated for that rak'ah, he does not return and must perform sajdah al-sahw. The commentary also discusses a dispute: if someone returns to the first sitting when he should not (i.e., when closer to standing), does the prayer become invalid? The mashhur view among Hanafis is that it does, because by returning he abandons the obligatory standing (which is a wajib). However, Ibn al-Humam argued that it does not invalidate because adding a small amount of standing does not invalidate the prayer; the sin is in abandoning the wajib, but the prayer remains valid. The hadith of Mughirah provides the sunnah basis for these rulings. The distinction between first and last sitting reflects the difference between fard (last sitting recitation) and wajib (first sitting recitation).

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in prayers of three or four rak'ahs, where the tashahhud is recited.
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting at the end of the prayer where the tashahhud and salawat are recited; it is a fard.
التقييد بالسجدة (al-taqyid bi al-sajdah): Committing to the prostration of the next rak'ah, i.e., having performed at least one sajdah of that rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person praying Dhuhr (4 rak'ahs) forgets the first tashahhud and begins to stand. At what point is it considered that he is closer to standing than to sitting?
A) When he lifts his hands for takbir.
B) When the first half of his body is upright (the upper body is straight).
C) When he has completed the standing (full straightening).
D) When he is half-standing (equal between sitting and standing).

Key Takeaway
The first tashahhud sitting is a wajib, the last is a fard, and the rules for returning depend on physical posture and commitment to the next prostration, with a valid intra-madhhab dispute on the invalidity of returning when closer to standing.

Ruling on Standing After Final Sitting and Adding Extra Rak'ahs
Explains the ruling when one stands after final sitting and adds extra rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for forgetfully standing after the final sitting and adding extra rak'ahs, and identify when the extra rak'ahs are emphatic due to the obligation of sajdat al-sahw.

Core Idea
When you prostrate for a fifth rak'ah after forgetting final sitting, your fard is complete; the extra two rak'ahs are nafl but sajdat al-sahw is wajib.

Forgetfulness in prayer often leads to confusion. One common scenario is standing after the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and adding an extra rak'ah. The Hanafi school distinguishes sharply between whether you have already prostrated for that extra rak'ah or not. This ruling not only clarifies what to do but also reveals an important principle: the extra rak'ahs are supererogatory and do not replace the sunnah, yet in certain cases they become emphatic because they carry the wajib sajdat al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note whether the person has prostrated for the fifth rak'ah or not. Before prostration, he returns and does taslim. After prostration, he continues to add a sixth rak'ah.
The ruling hinges on the moment of sajdah.
2
Determine the status of the added rak'ahs
The two extra rak'ahs after the fifth sajdah are nafl (supererogatory). Cutting them does not require qada, and they do not count as the post-sunnah of zuhr.
Nafl begun without intention does not need completion.
3
Understand the role of sajdat al-sahw
Because the fard was completed (by doing the fourth and fifth rak'ahs) but taslim was delayed, sajdat al-sahw becomes wajib. It is performed after the extra rak'ahs, before taslim.
Sajdat al-sahw compensates for the deficiency of leaving the fard in a non-sunnah manner.
4
Analyse why 'in sha'a' is omitted here
In the earlier case (standing without final sitting), the matn said 'adds a sixth if he wishes'. Here it says only 'adds a sixth' because the extra rak'ahs are more emphatic: cutting them would abandon the wajib sajdat al-sahw.
The difference shows that the obligation to preserve the wajib overrides the optional nature of the nafl.
5
Apply to other prayer types
For two-rak'ah prayers (Fajr), add a fourth. For four-rak'ah (Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha), add a sixth. For three-rak'ah (Maghrib), do not add because it becomes four.
The rule always yields two extra rak'ahs, except Maghrib where one extra is enough.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحول فرضه نفلاً وضم سادسةً إن شاء، وإن قعد الأخيرة ثم قام سهواً عاد ما لم يسجد للخامسة وسلّم، وإن سجد لها تم فرضه وضم سادسة، وسجد للسهو، والركعتان نفل، ولا قضاء لو قطع، ولا تنوبان عن سنة الظهر.

قوله: نفلاً؛ لأنه استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل إتمام أركان المكتوبة، ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض، والوجه فيه أنّ الركعة بسجدة صلاة حقيقة. [٢]قوله: سادسة؛ هذا في العصر والظهر، وفي الفجر يضم رابعة، وأما المغرب فلا يضم فيه؛ لأنه صار أربعاً. كذا قال الشرنبلالي في «إمداد الفتاح». [٣]قوله: فلم يجب عليه؛ فإنّ الذي يجب إتمامه هو النفلُ الذي شرع فيه قصداً كما مر. [٤]قوله: وسلّم؛ أي جالساً، وليست عليه إعادة التشهد، ولو سلم قائماً أساءَ ولم تفسد صلاته. كذا في «البناية». الثانية. [٥]قوله: سادسة؛ إن كانت الصلاة رباعيّة، ورابعة إن كانت ثنائية. [٦]قوله: وسجد للسهو؛ أي في الصورتين؛ لتأخير السلام في الأولى، وتركه في الثانية. [٧]قوله: والركعتان؛ أي اللتان صلاهما بعد القيام من القعدة الأخيرة. [٨]قوله: ولا قضاء؛ أي لو نقض هاتين الركعتين لا يلزمه قضاؤهما؛ لأنه نفل لم يشرع فيه قصدا، وما هذا شأنه لا يجب قضاؤه. [٩]قوله: ولا تنوبان؛ أي إن كانت هذه الواقعة في الظهر، فالركعتان زائدتان لا تقومان مقام السنة البعديَّة، بل عليه أن يؤديهما بعد الفراغ عنها.

فإن قلت لم قال قبل هذه المسألة: وضم سادسة إن شاء، وقال في هذه المسألة: وضم سادسة، ولم يقل: إن شاء مع أن الركعتين نفل في الصورتين بحيث لو قطع لا قضاء، فيكون في هذه المسألة ضم السادسة مقيداً بمشيئته. قلت: ضم السادسة في هذه المسألة آكد من ضم السادسة في تلك المسألة مع أنه لو قطع لا قضاء في المسألتين؛ وذلك لأن فرضه قد تم في هذه المسألة، لكن بتأخير السلام يجب سجود السهو في هاتين الركعتين، فسجود السهو لتدارك نقصان الفرض واجب في هاتين الركعتين، فلو قطع هاتين الركعتين بأن لا يسجد للسهو يلزم ترك الواجب.

[١]قوله: قبل هذه المسألة؛ أي فيما إذا قام تاركاً القعدة الأخيرة. [٢]قوله: فيكون؛ أي فيلزم أن يكون الضمّ في الصورة الثانية مقيداً بالمشيئة. [٣]قوله: قلت؛ حاصله: أنّ الصورتين وإن توافقا في كون الركعتين الزائدتين نفلاً، وفي عدم وجوب قضائهما إن نقضهما، لكن بينهما فرق من حيث أن ضم الركعة السادسة في الصورة الثانية أكد من ضمها في الأولى، فلهذا لم يذكر المشيئة هاهنا وذكرها في الأولى. [٤]قوله: قد تم؛ لعدم ترك القعدة الأخيرة. [٥]قوله: في ... الخ؛ بناءً على أن سجود السهو لا يكون خارج الصلاة. [٦]قوله: نقصان...الخ؛ وهو الخروج عن الفرض لا على الوجه المسنون، وهو خروجه بإصابة لفظ السلام بعد أربع ركعات، وقد ترك ذلك. [٧]قوله: يلزم....الخ؛ حاصله: أنه لو نقض هاتين الركعتين بناء على أن أداء النفل المظنون ونحوه وإتمامه غير لازم يلزم بقاء النقصان في الفرض؛ لعدم تداركه بسجود السهو، ولو جلس من القيام في هاتين الركعتين وأدّى سجدتي السهو يلزم عدم أداء السجدتين على الوجه المسنون، وهو كونهما في آخر الصلاة بعد التشهد، فلذا تأكد
His fard prayer turns into supererogatory, and he adds a sixth if he wishes. And if he sat for the last [sitting], then stood forgetfully, he returns as long as he has not prostrated for the fifth and he makes taslim. And if he prostrated for it, his fard is complete and he adds a sixth, and he performs prostration of forgetfulness. And the two rak'ahs are supererogatory, and there is no making up if he cuts it off, and they do not take the place of the sunnah of zuhr.

His statement: 'supererogatory' because his entry into the supererogatory was firmly established before completing the pillars of the obligatory prayer, and necessarily it removes him from the obligatory. The reason is that a rak'ah with a prostration is truly a prayer. [2] His statement: 'sixth' – this is in 'asr and zuhr; in fajr he adds a fourth; as for maghrib, he does not add because it has become four. Thus said al-Shurunbulali in 'Imdad al-Fattah'. [3] His statement: 'so it is not obligatory upon him' – for what must be completed is the supererogatory that one has intentionally begun, as previously mentioned. [4] His statement: 'and he makes taslim' – i.e., while sitting, and he does not have to repeat the tashahhud. If he made taslim standing, he does wrong and his prayer is not invalidated. Thus in al-Binayah. Second. [5] His statement: 'sixth' – if the prayer is four-rak'ah; and fourth if it is two-rak'ah. [6] His statement: 'and he performs prostration of forgetfulness' – i.e., in both cases: due to delaying the taslim in the first, and abandoning it in the second. [7] His statement: 'the two rak'ahs' – i.e., the two he performed after rising from the last sitting. [8] His statement: 'and there is no making up' – i.e., if he invalidates these two rak'ahs, he is not required to make them up because it is supererogatory that he did not intentionally begin, and that which is such is not required to be made up. [9] His statement: 'and they do not take the place' – i.e., if this incident occurred in zuhr, the two extra rak'ahs do not stand in place of the post-sunnah; rather he is to perform it after completing them.

If you say: Why did he say before this issue: 'and he adds a sixth if he wishes' and in this issue he said: 'and he adds a sixth' without saying 'if he wishes', whereas the two rak'ahs are supererogatory in both cases such that if he cuts off there is no making up, so in this issue the adding of the sixth would be restricted to his wish? I say: Adding the sixth in this issue is more emphatic than adding the sixth in that issue, even though cutting off has no making up in both issues; that is because his fard has been completed in this issue, but due to delaying the taslim, prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory in these two rak'ahs. So prostration of forgetfulness to compensate for the deficiency of the fard is obligatory in these two rak'ahs. So if he cuts off these two rak'ahs by not prostrating for forgetfulness, he would be abandoning the obligatory.

[1] His statement: 'before this issue' – i.e., in the case where he stood abandoning the last sitting. [2] His statement: 'so it would be' – i.e., then the adding in the second case would be restricted to his wish. [3] His statement: 'I say' – the gist: the two cases, although they agree that the two extra rak'ahs are supererogatory and that there is no obligation of making them up if he invalidates them, yet there is a difference in that adding the sixth rak'ah in the second case is more emphatic than adding in the first, so he did not mention the wish here and mentioned it in the first. [4] His statement: 'has been completed' – because he did not abandon the last sitting. [5] His statement: 'in ... etc.' – based on that prostration of forgetfulness is not outside the prayer. [6] His statement: 'deficiency ... etc.' – it is exiting from the fard not in the sunnah manner, which is his exiting by uttering the word 'salam' after four rak'ahs, and he has abandoned that. [7] His statement: 'he would be ... etc.' – its gist: that if he invalidates these two rak'ahs based on that performing and completing the presumed supererogatory and the like is not necessary, the deficiency in the fard remains because it was not compensated by prostration of forgetfulness. If he sits from standing in these two rak'ahs and performs the two prostrations of forgetfulness, he would not perform the two prostrations in the sunnah manner, which is that they are at the end of the prayer after tashahhud. Hence it is more emphatic.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling for a person who, after sitting for the final tashahhud, forgetfully stands up to add a fifth rak'ah. The matn states: if he has not yet prostrated for the fifth, he must return to sitting and make taslim. If he has prostrated for the fifth, his fard is complete and he adds a sixth rak'ah (making two extra rak'ahs total) which are supererogatory; he then performs prostration of forgetfulness. The commentary clarifies that these two rak'ahs are not substitutes for the post-sunnah of zuhr.

The author then addresses a subtle point: why in the earlier case (where he stood forgetting the final sitting) the text says 'adds a sixth if he wishes', but here it says simply 'adds a sixth' without the option. The answer is that in this case the extra rak'ahs are more emphatic because the fard was completed but the taslim was delayed, making prostration of forgetfulness obligatory to compensate for the deficiency. Thus cutting off these rak'ahs would mean abandoning an obligatory (wajib) act (the sajdat al-sahw), whereas in the first case cutting off meant only abandoning a supererogatory act with no further consequence.

The commentary uses principles: supererogatory acts begun without intention do not require completion; nafil begun with full intention requires completion. Sajdat al-sahw is wajib in this case to remedy the delay in taslim.

Key Terms
القعده الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, which includes the tashahhud and is a wajib according to Hanafis.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary acts of worship beyond the obligatory.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to correct errors in prayer, such as missing a wajib or delaying a fard.
تسليم (taslīm): The concluding salutation of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to end the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person forgetfully stands after the final sitting and prostrates for the fifth rak'ah, what is the status of the two extra rak'ahs he then adds?
A) They are obligatory (fard) and must be completed.
B) They are supererogatory (nafl) and cutting them does not require qada.
C) They are a substitute for the sunnah of Zuhr.
D) They invalidate the prayer if cut.

Key Takeaway
The extra rak'ahs added after forgetfully standing from the final sitting are supererogatory, require sajdat al-sahw, and do not count as the sunnah prayer.

Adding a Sixth Rak'ah in Sujud al-Sahw: Emphatic or Optional?
Explains omission of 'in shā'a' in one sujud al-sahw ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the ruling to add a sixth rak'ah is more emphatic in the case of delayed salam after completing the fard, and distinguish it from the case where the last sitting was omitted.

Core Idea
Adding the sixth rak'ah is wajib when sujud al-sahw must be performed properly after the fard is complete.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah examines a subtle wording difference in Al-Hidayah between two rulings on sujud al-sahw. In one case the author says 'and he adds a sixth if he wishes', while in another he simply says 'and he adds a sixth'. The commentator unpacks the legal reasoning behind this distinction, revealing how the status of the fard prayer affects the obligation of the extra rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Cases
Distinguish the case where the last sitting was forgotten (previous ruling) from the case where salam was delayed after completing the fard (this ruling). In both, the worshipper adds two rak'ahs then sits, but the rulings on adding a sixth differ.
In the first case, the fard is invalidated (according to Imam Muhammad); in the second, the fard is complete.
2
Understand the Legal Status of the Fard
Recognize that when the fard is complete, delaying salam creates a deficiency that must be rectified by sujud al-sahw. Sujud al-sahw becomes wajib in the two added rak'ahs.
3
Analyze the Necessity of the Sixth Rak'ah
If the worshipper cuts the two rak'ahs without sujud al-sahw, he leaves a wajib. If he sits after two and performs sujud al-sahw, it is not in the prescribed sunna manner. Hence he must add a sixth rak'ah to properly perform sujud al-sahw after the final tashahhud.
This makes adding the sixth more emphatic (ākid) than in the first case.
4
Apply the Distinction
Conclude that in the first case the deficiency is not rectifiable (prayer invalid for Muhammad), so adding the sixth is merely optional ('in shā'a'). In this case, it is necessary to safeguard the validity of sujud al-sahw, hence no conditional.
5
Note the Subsidiary Issue
The passage also clarifies that the two added rak'ahs do not substitute for the sunnah of zuhr because the Prophet performed the sunnah with an independent takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت لم قال قبل هذه المسألة: وضم سادسة إن شاء، وقال في هذه المسألة : وضم سادسة ، ولم يقل : إن شاء مع أن الركعتين نفل في الصورتين بحيث لو قطع لا قضاء، فيكون في هذه المسألة ضم السادسة مقيداً بمشيئته. " قلت : ضم السادسة في هذه المسألةِ آكد من ضم السادسة في تلك المسألة مع أنه لو قطع لا قضاءً في المسألتين ؛ وذلك لأن فرضه قد تم في هذه المسألة ، لكن بتأخير السلام يجب سجود السهو في هاتين الركعتين، فسجود السهو لتدارك نقصان الفرض واجب في هاتين الركعتين ، فلو قطع هاتين الركعتين بأن لا يسجد للسهو يلزم ترك الواجب. ولو جلس من القيام وسجد للسهو لم يؤد سجود السهو على الوجه المسنون ، فلا بُدَّ أن يضم سادسة، وجلس على الركعتين، وسجد للسهو بخلافِ تلك المسألة، فإنَّ الفرضية قد بطلت، فا ذكرنا من تدارك نقصان الفرض غير موجود هاهنا ، على أنَّ أصل الصَّلاةِ باطلة عند محمد، فَعُلِمَ أن ضَمَّ السادسة صيانة عن البطلان آكد في هذه المسألة ، فلهذا لم يقل إن شاء، وإنما قال : لا تنوبان عن سُنَّةِ الظهر ؛ لأنَّ النَّبي واظب عليها بتحريمة مبتدأة.
If you say: why did he say before this issue: 'and he adds a sixth if he wishes' and in this issue he said: 'and he adds a sixth' and did not say 'if he wishes' despite the two rak'ahs being supererogatory in both cases such that if he cuts them there is no making up? So in this issue adding the sixth is conditional upon his wish? I say: adding the sixth in this issue is more emphatic than adding the sixth in that issue even though if he cuts there is no making up in both issues; that is because his obligatory (prayer) has been completed in this issue, but by delaying the salam, sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory in these two rak'ahs. So sujud al-sahw to rectify the deficiency of the obligatory prayer is wajib in these two rak'ahs. So if he cuts these two rak'ahs by not performing sujud al-sahw, he would be leaving a wajib. And if he sits down from standing and performs sujud al-sahw, he would not have performed sujud al-sahw in the sunna manner. So he must add a sixth, then sit after the two rak'ahs and perform sujud al-sahw. Unlike that issue, for there the obligatory status has been invalidated, so what we mentioned of rectifying the deficiency of the obligatory is not present here. Moreover, the original prayer is invalid according to Muhammad. So it is known that adding the sixth as a safeguard against invalidity is more emphatic in this issue, therefore he did not say 'if he wishes'. And he said: 'they do not serve as the sunna of zuhr' because the Prophet persistently observed it with an independent opening takbir.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of a specific ruling in sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The commentator addresses a subtle difference in wording between two rulings from the matn. In the first ruling (concerning a case where the worshipper forgot the last sitting), the author said 'and he adds a sixth if he wishes' (ضم سادسة إن شاء), using the conditional 'if he wishes'. In the present ruling (concerning a case where the worshipper delayed the salam after completing the fard), the author said only 'and he adds a sixth' (ضم سادسة) without the conditional. The questioner asks why the difference, since in both cases the two extra rak'ahs are nafal (supererogatory) and if the worshipper cuts them there is no qada (making up). The commentator explains that adding the sixth is more emphatic in the second case. Why? Because in the second case, the fard (obligatory) prayer has been properly completed (the last sitting was performed), but by delaying the salam, a deficiency occurs that must be rectified by sujud al-sahw. The sujud al-sahw becomes wajib in those two rak'ahs. If the worshipper cuts them by not performing sujud al-sahw, he would be omitting a wajib. Moreover, if he were to sit down after the two rak'ahs and perform sujud al-sahw, he would not be performing the sujud al-sahw in the prescribed manner (after the proper final tashahhud). Therefore, he must add a sixth rak'ah so that the sujud al-sahw is performed at the end of the prayer. In contrast, in the first ruling (where the worshipper forgot the last sitting), the fard itself has been invalidated (because standing up without the last sitting invalidates the fard according to Muhammad, or at least the obligatory description is lost). Thus, there is no deficiency in the fard to rectify; the original prayer is even invalid according to Muhammad. Hence, adding the sixth is less emphatic, so the author allowed discretion with 'if he wishes'. The passage also touches on another point: the two added rak'ahs cannot substitute for the sunnah of zuhr because the Prophet performed the sunnah with an independent opening takbir (tahrimah), not as part of the fard.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): The two prostrations performed to rectify forgetfulness that occurs in prayer.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The initial takbir (Allāhu Akbar) that begins the prayer and renders it sacred.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author omit 'in shā'a' (if he wishes) in the ruling about adding a sixth rak'ah in the case where the worshipper delays the salam after completing the four fard rak'ahs?
A) Because adding the sixth is not a recommended act in that case.
B) Because the fard is invalid, so there is no need for discretion.
C) Because adding the sixth is more emphatic due to the wajib nature of sujud al-sahw in those two rak'ahs.
D) Because the worshipper must add a sixth rak'ah only if he wishes to perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Adding a sixth rak'ah is necessary (wajib) when sujud al-sahw must be performed after completing the fard and delaying salam, because the sujud al-sahw is wajib in those added rak'ahs and must be performed in the sunna manner.

Adding a Sixth Rak'ah and Sujud al-Sahw: Do Extra Rak'ahs Substitute for Sunnah?
Ruling with proof on adding a sixth rak'ah and sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why adding a sixth rak'ah is wajib when one mistakenly stands for a fifth, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether two extra rak'ahs can fulfill the sunnah of zuhr.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw must be at the end of prayer; adding a sixth rak'ah is necessary to avoid invalidity, and the extra rak'ahs do not count as the sunnah.

In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, if one mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah and then sits and performs sujud al-sahw, the sujud is invalid because it occurs mid-prayer. The Hanafi school rules that a sixth rak'ah must be added to position the sujud at the end. Furthermore, a dispute arises whether these two extra rak'ahs can serve as the sunnah of zuhr. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize that standing for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard disrupts the intended sequence. The prayer now has five rak'ahs.
2
Explain why the sujud al-sahw after the fifth is invalid
Sujud al-sahw must occur at the end of the prayer. Performing it after the fifth rak'ah places it in the middle, making it invalid.
The sahw occurs mid-prayer, not after completion.
3
Describe the solution: add a sixth rak'ah
To rectify, one must add a sixth rak'ah so that the sujud al-sahw is performed after the final tashahhud, at the true end of the prayer. This is wajib.
Adding the sixth is more emphasized to protect against invalidity.
4
Analyze the dispute on substitution for sunnah
Some Hanafi scholars (Ibn Sama'ah from Muhammad) held that the two extra rak'ahs can substitute for the sunnah of zuhr. Others (Fakhr al-Islam, Qadi Khan, and the relied-upon view) said they do not.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, based on different interpretations of the Prophet's practice.
5
Present the dalil and tarjih
The Prophet consistently performed the sunnah of zuhr with an independent tahrimah (intention). Therefore, two rak'ahs lacking that independence cannot fulfill the sunnah. This view is adopted in al-Hidayah.
The dalil is a hadith on the Prophet's constancy (wujub of independent tahrimah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو جلس من القيام وسجد للسهو لم يؤد سجود السهو على الوجه المسنون ، فلا بُدَّ أن يضم سادسة، وجلس على الركعتين، وسجد للسهو بخلافِ تلك المسألة، فإنَّ الفرضية قد بطلت ، فـا ذكرنا من تدارك نقصان الفرض غير موجود هاهنا ، على أنَّ أصل الصَّلاةِ باطلة عند محمد، فَعُلِمَ أن ضَمَّ السَّادسة صيانة عن البطلان آكد في هذه المسألة ، فلهذا لم يقل إن شاء، وإنما قال : لا تنوبان عن سُنَّةِ الظهر ؛ لأنَّ النَّبي واظب عليها بتحريمة مبتدأة.
هاهنا أن يَضُمَّ ركعة أُخرى ليقع سجود السهو في آخر الصلاة، ويتدارك نقصان الفرض.
قوله على..الخ؛ علاوة على ما قرر سابقاً، وحاصله: أن تدارك نقصان الفرض غير موجود هناك؛ لبطلان الفرضية اتفاقاً، ولبطلان أصل الصلاة عند محمد لمّا مرّ أنّ عنده يبطل أصلُ الصلاة عند بطلان وصف الفرضية.
قوله فعلم؛ تفريع على ما بين من الفرق بين الصورتين.
قوله لأن النبي..الخ؛ اختلف فيه: فقال بعض المشايخ: إنهما تنوبان سنة الظهر، وهو رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد؛ لأنه أتى بالركعتين في موضع السنة، فيقومان مقامهما، كما قال شمس الأئمة الحلوائي له فيمن صلّى آخر الليل ركعتين بنية التطوع على ظنّ أنّ الفجر لم يطلع، فظهر أنه كان قد طلع، إنهما يجزئانه عن سنة الفجر. وذهب فخر الإسلام وقاضي خان وجماعة من المشايخ إلى عدم الإنابة وصححه في «الهداية»، وعللوه بأنّ مواظبة النبي بعد الظهر كانت بتحريمة مستقلة لا مبنية على غيرها، فلا تتأدّى السنّة بما هو ناقص غير مضمون، وغير مستقل. كذا في «البناية».
And if he sits after standing and performs sujud al-sahw, he has not performed sujud al-sahw in the sunnah manner, so he must add a sixth, and he sat at two rak'ahs and performed sujud al-sahw contrary to that issue, for the obligatory nature has been nullified, so what we mentioned of compensating the deficiency of the obligatory is not present here, whereas indeed the original prayer is invalid according to Muhammad. So it is known that adding the sixth is more emphasized for protection from invalidity in this issue, therefore he did not say 'if he wishes', but rather said: 'They do not substitute for the sunnah of zuhr because the Prophet continuously performed them with an initial tahrimah.'
Here he should add another rak'ah so that sujud al-sahw occurs at the end of the prayer and he compensates the deficiency of the obligatory.
His statement: 'on..etc.' is in addition to what was established previously, and its summary: that compensating the deficiency of the obligatory is not present there due to the consensus that the obligatory nature is nullified, and due to the invalidity of the original prayer according to Muhammad, because as has passed, according to him the original prayer becomes invalid when the attribute of obligatory is nullified.
His statement: 'so it is known' is a branch on what was explained of the difference between the two cases.
His statement: 'because the Prophet..etc.' there is disagreement about it: some scholars said they substitute for the sunnah of zuhr, which is a narration from Ibn Sama'ah from Muhammad, because he performed two rak'ahs in the place of the sunnah, so they stand in their place, as Shams al-A'imma al-Halwa'i said about the one who prayed two rak'ahs at the end of the night with the intention of voluntary prayer thinking that dawn had not risen, and it became clear that it had risen, that they suffice him for the sunnah of fajr. And Fakhr al-Islam, Qadi Khan, and a group of scholars held the opinion of non-substitution, and it was declared sahih in al-Hidayah, and they reasoned that the Prophet's constancy after zuhr was with an independent tahrimah not built on something else, so the sunnah cannot be performed by something deficient, not guaranteed, and not independent. Thus in al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of a person who in a four-rak'ah fard prayer mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah, then sits after two prostrations and performs sujud al-sahw. The text states that this does not fulfill the sunnah method of sujud al-sahw because the sahw must occur at the end of the prayer, not in the middle. Therefore, one must add a sixth rak'ah so that the sujud al-sahw is performed correctly at the end of the prayer. The commentary clarifies the difference between this case and the earlier one (where the person sat after the fourth rak'ah): in this case, the attribute of obligatory (fardiyyah) has been nullified by the extra standing, and according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the entire prayer becomes invalid. Thus, adding the sixth rak'ah is more necessary to salvage the prayer. The author of al-Hidayah uses this to explain why the matn says 'they do not substitute for the sunnah of zuhr' rather than giving an option. The commentary then discusses a dispute among Hanafi scholars about whether these two additional rak'ahs (the fifth and sixth) can fulfill the sunnah of zuhr. Some, citing a narration from Ibn Sama'ah, say they do substitute because the person performed them in the place of the actual sunnah. Others, including Fakhr al-Islam and Qadi Khan, say they do not, because the Prophet's custom was to pray the sunnah with an independent intention (tahrimah) not built upon the fard. The relied-upon position is that they do not substitute, as confirmed in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness errors during prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that initiates the prayer and marks its beginning as a sanctified act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, sits after two prostrations, and performs sujud al-sahw, why must he add a sixth rak'ah?
A) Because the fifth rak'ah is invalid and must be replaced.
B) Because sujud al-sahw must occur at the end of the prayer, and without a sixth rak'ah it would occur in the middle.
C) Because the prayer becomes a six-rak'ah prayer by default.
D) Because the imam must lead six rak'ahs in congregation.

Key Takeaway
When one mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard, a sixth must be added to ensure sujud al-sahw is at the end, and these two extra rak'ahs do not count as the sunnah.

Muqtadi's Obligation When Imam Stands for Fifth Rak'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on follower's duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the follower's duty when the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The follower must make up the extra two rak'ahs if invalidated because he intended them; the imam does not.

This passage examines a specific scenario where the imam, after the tashahhud, mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah. The follower who joins him in those extra rak'ahs faces a unique ruling. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Yusuf (supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson will dissect their arguments and the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam fulfills the last tashahhud (qa'da) but then stands for a fifth rak'ah by mistake. The follower chooses to follow him in these extra two rak'ahs.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf (and a narration from Abu Hanifa) holds that the follower must pray only these two extra rak'ahs. If he invalidates them, he must make them up (qada).
The follower's deliberate intention (qasd) distinguishes him from the imam.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the follower prays a total of six rak'ahs (the four fard plus two extra) and if he invalidates the extra two, he does not make them up.
Muhammad considers the follower's situation analogous to the imam's.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the follower voluntarily followed the imam in error, thus intending the extra rak'ahs. The imam did not intend them, so they are treated differently. Muhammad argues that since the follower is in the same prayer as the imam, the same rule applies.
The key distinction is qasd (intention) in starting the extra rak'ahs.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Yusuf, as confirmed by Fath al-Qadir and other later Hanafi authorities. Therefore, the follower must make up the extra rak'ahs if he invalidates them.
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text

ومن اقتدى به فيهما صلاهما ولو أفسد قضاهما وعند محمد يصلّي ستّا ولو أفسد لا يقضى.
قوله : ومن اقتدى... الخ ; يعني لو اقتدى رجلٌ بمن قام إلى الخامسة بعد القعدة في هاتين الركعتين الزائدتين يجب عليه أن يصليهما لا غير؛ لأنه يستحكم خروجه عن الفرض بإتمام الأركان، فلا يلزم المؤتم غير هذا الشفع ولو أفسده المؤتم يلزم عليه قضاؤه؛ لأنه شرع فيه قصداً بخلاف الإمام، فإنّه لا يجب عليه قضاؤه إن أفسد؛ لأنه لم يشرع فيه قصدا، وهذا عند أبي يوسف له، وذكر في «الخلاصة» قول أبي حنيفة له أيضا.
