قوله : وعند محمد الله يصلي سنًّا ; هو يعتبر حاله بحال الإمام، فيقول كما أنّ الإمامَ صلّى ستّا، ولو أفسد الركعتين لا يقضي، كذلك المقتدى به في هاتين الركعتين يُصلّي سنًّا، ولا يقضي عند الإفساد، وقد مرّ جوابه فيما مرّ، والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف له، كما في «فتح القدير».
And whoever follows him in them, he prays them, and if he invalidates them, he makes them up; and according to Muhammad, he prays six, and if he invalidates, he does not make up.
His statement: 'And whoever follows..etc.' means if a man follows one who stood to the fifth after the tashahhud in these two extra rak'ahs, he must pray them alone, because he [the imam] has solidified his exit from the fard by completing the pillars, so the follower is only obliged to do this pair. And if the follower invalidates them, he must make them up because he intended them deliberately, unlike the imam, who does not have to make them up if he invalidates because he did not intend them deliberately. This is according to Abu Yusuf, and it is mentioned in al-Khulasa that Abu Hanifa also said this.
His statement: 'prays them..etc.' And if he follows him in the case of omitting the last tashahhud, the follower prays six. Thus in al-Muhit.
His statement: 'And according to Muhammad he prays six' He considers his situation like that of the imam, so he says: just as the imam prayed six, and if he invalidates the two rak'ahs he does not make up, likewise the follower in these two rak'ahs prays six and does not make up when invalidated. And his response has passed earlier. And the fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf's statement, as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad) regarding the follower's obligation when the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah after the tashahhud. The matn states that the follower must pray these two extra rak'ahs; if he invalidates them, he must make them up (qada). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, the follower prays six rak'ahs total (the four fard plus two extra) and if he invalidates the extra two, he does not make them up. The commentary explains the reasoning: according to Abu Yusuf (and also a narration from Abu Hanifa), the follower intentionally began the extra rak'ahs (since he voluntarily followed the imam in the error), so if he invalidates them, he must make them up. The imam did not intend them, so he does not make up. According to Muhammad, he considers the follower's situation identical to the imam's: both are in the same position, so the follower prays six and does not make up. However, the fatwa is on the opinion of Abu Yusuf. The commentary also mentions a second scenario: if the imam omits the last tashahhud entirely and stands for the fifth, the follower must pray six rak'ahs (four fard and two extra) according to Abu Yusuf; the view of Muhammad is that he prays six as well but does not make up if he invalidates. The relied-upon position for this scenario is also the view of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadi): A person praying behind an imam as a follower (ma'mum).
قضاء (qada): Making up a prayer that was invalidated or missed after its prescribed time.
قصد (qasd): Deliberate intention; the mental state of choosing to do an act with volition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He does not make them up because he was following.
B) He makes them up because he intended them deliberately.
C) He must repeat the entire prayer.
D) He prays six rak'ahs and does not make up.

Key Takeaway
The follower must make up the extra two rak'ahs if invalidated because his deliberate intention (qasd) distinguishes his case from the imam's; this is the mufta bihi position.

Building Additional Rak'ahs After Sujud al-Sahw: Valid but Disapproved
Clarifies that sujud al-sahw prevents building further rak'ahs without new intention, but if done, the prayer is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building additional rak'ahs after sujud al-sahw and explain why it is valid despite being makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw must be at the prayer's end; adding rak'ahs after it places the sujud in the middle, but the prayer remains valid.

This passage from `Umdat al-Ri`ayah clarifies a scenario where a person prays two rak'ahs, forgets, performs sujud al-sahw, and then wants to add more rak'ahs without a new takbir. The matn states it is not recommended, but if done, the prayer is valid. The commentary explains the reason: sujud al-sahw belongs at the end, not the middle. Understanding this helps avoid confusion about the status of sujud al-sahw and the continuity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is building (adding rak'ahs) after sujud al-sahw. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disapproved) but if done, the prayer is sahih (valid).
The ruling applies to both nafl and fard prayers.
2
Understand the reason for disapproval
Sujud al-sahw is meant to be at the end of the prayer. Adding rak'ahs after it places the sujud in the middle, which is not its proper place.
The proper place (mahall) of sujud al-sahw is the end of the prayer.
3
Recognize the principle of tahrimah
The original intention (tahrimah) remains valid even after sujud al-sahw, so the prayer is not broken.
Tahrimah is the initial takbir that sanctifies the prayer.
4
Note the remedy
If one builds, they should repeat the sujud al-sahw at the end of the newly added rak'ahs.
The commentary ends with 'wa yu'id' indicating the need to repeat the sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَن تنفل ركعتين وسها فسجد لا يبني عليها فإن بني صح.
قوله : تنفل ركعتين... الخ ; ذكر التنفّل اتفاقي، فإنّ الحكم في الفرض كذلك، وحاصل المسألة: أنه إذا صلى ركعتين فرضاً كان أو نفلاً، وسها فيهما فسجد للسهو بعد السلام أو قبله في آخر صلاته، ثمّ أرادَ بناءً شفع عليه من غير تجديد التحريمة، لم يكن له ذلك لاستلزامه وقوع سجود السهو في أثناء الصلاة، مع أن موضعه هو آخرها لا وسطها.
قوله : فإن بني ; أي فإن اختار البناءَ صحت صلاته؛ لبقاء التحريمة، ويعيد
Whoever prays two rak'ahs of nafl and forgets and prostrates (forgets), he does not build upon them; if he builds, it is valid.
His statement: 'prays two rak'ahs of nafl..etc.' Mentioning nafl is coincidental, for the same ruling applies to fard. The summary of the issue: if one prays two rak'ahs, whether fard or nafl, and forgets in them and prostrates for forgetfulness after the salam or before it at the end of his prayer, then he wants to build a pair upon it without renewing the tahrimah, he does not have that because it necessitates that the sujud al-sahw occurs in the middle of the prayer, whereas its place is at its end, not its middle.
His statement: 'if he builds' meaning if he chooses to build, his prayer is valid due to the remaining tahrimah, and he repeats...
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding building additional rak'ahs upon a set of two rak'ahs after performing sujud al-sahw. The matn states that if a person prays two rak'ahs of nafl and forgets and performs sujud al-sahw, he should not build another pair onto these two rak'ahs; but if he does build, the prayer is valid. The commentary explains that the ruling is not specific to nafl; it applies equally to fard prayer. The reason it is disapproved is that the sujud al-sahw is meant to be at the end of the prayer; if one builds more rak'ahs after it, the sujud would then fall in the middle, which is not its proper place. However, if one nevertheless adds rak'ahs without renewing the tahrimah (initial takbir), the prayer is still valid because the original intention (tahrimah) is not broken by the sujud al-sahw; it remains in effect. The phrase 'wa yu'id' at the end suggests that he should repeat the sujud al-sahw at the end of the new prayer. This is consistent with the principle that a new tahrimah is not required for additional rak'ahs if the prayer is continuous.

Key Terms
بناء (bina): Adding additional rak'ahs to a prayer without renewing the tahrimah.
تنفل (tanafful): Performing voluntary (nafl) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not allowed at all; the prayer is invalid.
B) It is allowed and recommended.
C) It is not recommended, but if done, the prayer is valid and the sujud al-sahw should be repeated at the end.
D) It is allowed only if he makes a new intention.

Key Takeaway
Building additional rak'ahs after sujud al-sahw is valid but makruh tanzih; the sujud should be repeated at the end.

The Follower and the Imam’s Extra Rak'ahs: Intent and Liability
Ruling on the follower's following in extra rak'ahs with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower when the imam adds extra rak'ahs, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and apply the distinction between intentional and unintentional entry to determine liability.

Core Idea
The follower must make up extra rak'ahs because he entered them intentionally; the imam does not.

What happens when an imam inadvertently prays extra rak'ahs? Is the follower bound to follow? And if the follower spoils those rak'ahs, must he make them up? This lesson unpacks a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute rooted in the concept of qasd (intention). By understanding this, you will see how the Hanafi school uses niyyah to distinguish between the imam's and the follower's obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam, after the final sitting (qa'da), mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah. The follower now faces a choice: follow or not. The passage addresses when the follower (muqtadi) does follow into those extra rak'ahs.
The imam's extra rak'ahs are not part of the original prayer; they are an error.
2
State the base ruling (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the follower must perform only those two extra rak'ahs (not more). If he spoils them (e.g., by nullifying his prayer), he must make them up (qada).
The ruling is wajib: following the imam in the extra rak'ahs is obligatory, and making them up if spoiled is also obligatory.
3
Understand the reasoning (intentional entry)
The follower entered the extra rak'ahs intentionally (shara'a fihi qasdan) because he deliberately chose to follow the imam. Therefore, he bears full responsibility for them. In contrast, the imam did not intend to add rak'ahs; he erred, so he is not liable to make them up if spoiled.
This is the key distinction: qasd (intent) creates liability.
4
Compare with Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad argues that the follower's state should mirror the imam's: just as the imam prays six rak'ahs (original two + four extra? Actually, Muhammad says the follower prays six total) and does not make up if spoiled, so too the follower should pray six and not make up. He analogizes the follower to the imam, ignoring the difference in intention.
Muhammad's position: follower prays six rak'ahs; no qada if spoiled.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (fatwa) is that of Abu Yusuf (and Abu Hanifa). The follower must make up the extra rak'ahs if spoiled because he entered them with intent.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir confirm this tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من اقتدى به فيهما صلاهما، ولو أفسد قضاهما، وعند محمد يصلّي ستّا، ولو أفسد لا يقضى.
قوله: ومن اقتدى... الخ؛ يعني لو اقتدى رجلٌ بمن قام إلى الخامسة بعد القعدة في هاتين الركعتين الزائدتين يجب عليه أن يصليهما لا غير؛ لأنه يستحكم خروجه عن الفرض بإتمام الأركان، فلا يلزم المؤتم غير هذا الشفع. ولو أفسده المؤتم يلزم عليه قضاؤه؛ لأنه شرع فيه قصداً بخلاف الإمام، فإنّه لا يجب عليه قضاؤه إن أفسد؛ لأنه لم يشرع فيه قصدا، وهذا عند أبي يوسف، وذكر في «الخلاصة» قول أبي حنيفة أيضا.

[٣] قوله: وعند محمد يصلّي ستّا؛ هو يعتبر حاله بحال الإمام، فيقول كما أنّ الإمام صلّى ستّا ولو أفسد الركعتين لا يقضي، كذلك المقتدى به في هاتين الركعتين يصلّي ستّا ولا يقضي عند الإفساد، والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف، كما في «فتح القدير».
Whoever follows him in them (the two extra rak'ahs) prays them, and if he spoils them he makes them up. According to Muhammad, he prays six (rak'ahs) and if he spoils them he does not make them up. His saying: 'Whoever follows him in them...' meaning: if a man follows someone who stood up for a fifth after the sitting in these two extra rak'ahs, he must pray only them; because his exit from the obligatory (prayer) is confirmed by completing the pillars, so nothing other than this pair is binding on the follower. And if the follower spoils them, he must make them up because he entered into them intentionally, unlike the imam, who does not have to make them up if he spoils them because he did not enter into them intentionally. This is according to Abu Yusuf, and in al-Khulasa the saying of Abu Hanifa is also mentioned. [2] His saying: 'prays them...' etc.; and if he follows him in the case of omitting the last sitting, the follower prays six. Thus in al-Muhit. [3] His saying: 'according to Muhammad he prays six'; he considers his state like that of the imam, saying: just as the imam prays six and if he spoils the two rak'ahs he does not make them up, likewise the follower in these two rak'ahs prays six and does not make them up if he spoils them. And the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf, as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a follower (muqtadi) who follows an imam who, after the final sitting (qa'da), stands up for additional rak'ahs (e.g., a fifth and sixth). The ruling: the follower must perform those extra rak'ahs. If he spoils them (e.g., by nullifying his prayer), he must make them up. This is because he entered them intentionally (qasdan). The imam, however, did not enter them intentionally, so he does not have to make them up. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree on this. Imam Muhammad holds a different view: the follower should pray six rak'ahs total (i.e., the original two plus the two extra plus two more? Actually, he says 'sitta' meaning six, implying a different calculation) and if he spoils them he does not make them up, analogous to the imam. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf, as stated in al-Hidayah and other works. The commentary also notes that if the imam omitted the final sitting, the follower prays six rak'ahs.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer who follows the imam.
قضاء (qaḍā’): Making up a prayer after its time or after nullification.
شرع فيه قصداً (shara‘a fīhi qaṣdan): He entered into it intentionally, i.e., with deliberate intention to perform those rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He does not have to make them up because the imam does not.
B) He must make them up because he entered them intentionally.
C) He must repeat the entire prayer.
D) He must perform six rak'ahs instead.

Key Takeaway
The follower's intention distinguishes his liability from the imam's; thus he must make up extra rak'ahs if spoiled.

Building on a Prayer After Sajdat al-Sahw
Ruling on adding rak'ahs after sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building additional rak'ahs after sajdat al-sahw and explain the legal reason (ta'lil) that leads to the repetition of sajdat al-sahw.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-sahw belongs at the end; building after it voids it and requires repetition.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in prayer: a person performs sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) after two rak'ahs, then wishes to add more rak'ahs without renewing the opening takbir. The Hanafi school rules that this building is not allowed, but if done, the prayer remains valid while the sajdat al-sahw must be repeated at the end of the extended prayer. The ruling hinges on the principle that sajdat al-sahw has a fixed place—at the conclusion of the prayer—and cannot be placed in the middle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The person prays two rak'ahs (fard or nafl), forgets, and performs sajdat al-sahw (before or after salam). The default ruling: he may not build additional rak'ahs without a new takbir because sajdat al-sahw must be at the end of the prayer, not in the middle.
The mention of 'supererogatory' is incidental; the ruling applies to obligatory prayer as well.
2
Identify the exception and its consequence
If he chooses to build (add rak'ahs), the prayer is valid because the tahrima remains intact. However, the previous sajdat al-sahw becomes void due to its occurrence in the middle of the now-extended prayer. He must repeat sajdat al-sahw at the end.
There is a difference of opinion on repetition; the correct view is he repeats.
3
Understand the ta'lil (legal reasoning)
The prohibition and the voiding of the previous sajdat al-sahw are based on the fixed position of sajdat al-sahw: its place is at the end of the prayer, not in the middle. The tahrima remains, so the prayer is not invalidated, but the wajib compensation (sajdat al-sahw) becomes due again.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the prayer's validity and the compensation for forgetfulness are distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من تنفل ركعتين وسها فسجد لا يبني عليها، فإن بني صح.
قوله: تنفل ركعتين...الخ؛ ذكر التنفل اتفاقي، فإن الحكم في الفرض كذلك. وحاصل المسألة: أنه إذا صلى ركعتين فرضاً كان أو نفلاً، وسها فيهما فسجد للسهو بعد السلام أو قبله في آخر صلاته، ثم أراد بناء شفع عليه من غير تجديد التحريمة، لم يكن له ذلك لاستلزامه وقوع سجود السهو في أثناء الصلاة، مع أن موضعه هو آخرها لا وسطها.
قوله: فإن بني؛ أي فإن اختار البناء صحت صلاته؛ لبقاء التحريمة، ويعيد سجود السهو في آخر صلاته؛ لبطلان السابق بوقوعه في وسط الصلاة، هو الصحيح، وقيل: لا يعيد. كذا في «الهداية» و«البناية».
Whoever prays two rak'ahs of supererogatory (prayer) and forgets and prostrates (for sahw), he may not build upon them, but if he does build, it is valid. His saying: 'prays two rak'ahs supererogatory...' etc.; the mention of supererogatory is incidental, for the ruling is the same in obligatory. The summary of the issue: When a person prays two rak'ahs, obligatory or supererogatory, and forgets in them and performs sajdat al-sahw after the salam or before in the end of his prayer, then he wishes to build upon that a pair without renewing the takbir, he may not do so because it entails that the sajdat al-sahw occurs in the midst of the prayer, whereas its place is at the end, not the middle. His saying: 'but if he builds'; i.e., if he chooses to build, his prayer is valid because the takbir remains, and he repeats the sajdat al-sahw at the end of his prayer because the previous one is nullified by its occurrence in the middle of the prayer. This is the correct view, and it is said: he does not repeat. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person who prays two rak'ahs (whether fard or nafl) and during the prayer forgets and performs sajdat al-sahw either before or after the salam. The ruling is that he cannot then add additional rak'ahs (building upon them) without renewing the opening takbir (tahrima). This is because sajdat al-sahw is meant to be performed at the end of the prayer, not in the middle. If he does build (i.e., adds rak'ahs with the same tahrima), his prayer is valid because the tahrima is still intact, but the sajdat al-sahw he performed earlier becomes void because it occurred in the middle of the prayer; he must repeat it at the end of his new prayer. There is a difference of opinion on whether he needs to repeat it: the correct view according to the author is that he must repeat it. This ruling applies whether the prayer was obligatory or supererogatory.

Key Terms
بناء (binā’): Adding further rak'ahs onto the same prayer without a new takbir.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that enters one into the state of prayer.
سجد السهو (sajdat al-sahw): The prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone prays two rak'ahs, performs sajdat al-sahw after salam, then adds two more rak'ahs without a new takbir, what is the ruling?
A) The added rak'ahs are invalid and the whole prayer is void.
B) The prayer is valid and the sajdat al-sahw is fine.
C) The prayer is valid but the sajdat al-sahw must be repeated at the end of the added rak'ahs.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer because he interrupted it.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw must be at the end of the prayer; building after it shifts its place, voiding it and requiring a new sajdat al-sahw.

Suspended Exit: The Ruling on Salam When Sajdat al-Sahw is Due
Ruling on salam with sajdat al-sahw due, laughing in prayer, and iqamah intent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of suspended exit (mawqūf) when salam is said while sajdat al-sahw is due, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf from Muhammad.

Core Idea
Salam with sajdat al-sahw due: exit is suspended until prostration is performed or omitted.

In this passage, the author addresses a nuanced situation: a person in prayer who has missed a sajdat al-sahw says the salam. Does the salam end the prayer immediately? The Hanafi school presents a subtle answer: the exit is suspended, depending on what happens next. The passage also briefly touches on the effects of laughing during prayer and intending to perform the full prayer (iqamah) while in this suspended state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings in the passage
The passage states three rulings: (1) the effect of salam when sajdat al-sahw is due, (2) invalidation of wudu by loud laughter (qahqaha), and (3) the prayer becoming four rak'ahs by intention of iqamah after salam but before prostration.
2
Differentiate the positions on the first ruling
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the exit is suspended (mawqūf). Muhammad holds that the salam does not exit the prayer at all. Understand the reasoning behind each.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rely on the hadith 'تحليلها التسليم' and interpret its application here as suspended. Muhammad argues that sajdat al-sahw must be performed within the prayer's sanctity, so salam cannot exit. Consider how they reconcile the general principle with this case.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and others.
4
Apply the concept of suspension to the other rulings
The passage links the suspended state to the validity of following him in prayer, the nullification of wudu by laughter, and the change in the number of rak'ahs by intention of iqamah. Explain how these are connected.
The suspended state allows for continued actions like prostration and intention changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلام من عليه السهو يخرجه عنها موقوفاً حتى يصح الاقتداء به، ويبطل وضوؤه بالقهقهة، ويصير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة.
قوله: سلام من... الخ؛ يعني إذا سلّم في آخر الصلاة وعليه سجود السهو، يخرجه السلام عن تلك الصلاة خروجاً موقوفاً، ومعناه: أنه يتوقف على ظهور عاقبته، ولا يحكم بخروجه، فإن سجد بعد ذلك للسهو تبين أنه لم يخرجه، وإن لم يسجد تبين أنه أخرجه من وقت وجوده. وقيل: معنى التوقف أنه وإن كان يخرجه من كل وجه لكن على احتمال أن يعود إلى حرمتها بالسجود، وبعد خروجه منها، فإن سجد عاد وإلا فلا. وصحح في «البدائع» المعنى الأول بناءً على أن التحريمة واحدة، فإذا بطلت لا تعود إلا بإعادة، ولم توجد. وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد: هو خارج سجد أو لم يسجد؛ لأن عنده سلام من عليه السهو لا يخرجه عن الصلاة أصلاً؛ لأنها وجبت جبر النقصان، فلا بد أن يكون في إحرام الصلاة. وجوابه من قبلهما: أن السلام محلل في نفسه؛ لحديث: «تحليلها التسليم»، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره، وإنما لا يعمل هاهنا لحاجته إلى أداء السجدة، فلا يظهر بدونها، ولا حاجة عند اعتبار عدم العود. كذا في «الهداية» وشروحها.
[٢] قوله: بنية الإقامة؛ أي بعد السلام قبل السجود، أما إن كان قبل السلام فلا شك أنه يصير فرضه أربعاً اتفاقاً؛ لأنه لم يخرج من حرمة الصلاة اتفاقاً، وكذا بعد
The salutation of one who has (the obligation of) sajdat al-sahw removes him from it (the prayer) in a suspended manner until following him becomes valid, and his ablution is invalidated by loud laughter, and his obligatory (prayer) becomes four by intention of iqamah.
His saying: 'Salutation of one who...' etc.; meaning: When one says the salam at the end of the prayer while sajdat al-sahw is due, the salam removes him from that prayer with a suspended exit. Its meaning: it depends on the outcome; he is not judged to have exited. If he then prostrates for sahw, it becomes clear that it did not remove him; if he does not prostrate, it becomes clear that it removed him from the time of its occurrence. And it is said the meaning of suspension is that although it removes him in every respect, there is a possibility that he will return to its sanctity by the prostration, and after exiting from it, if he prostrates he returns, otherwise not. In al-Bada'i', the first meaning is preferred based on the fact that the tahrima is one; if it is nullified, it does not return except by renewal, which did not occur. All this according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He is out whether he prostrates or not, because according to him the salam of one who has sajdat al-sahw due does not remove him from the prayer at all, because it (the sajdat al-sahw) is obligatory to compensate the deficiency, so it must be within the state of prayer. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) response: The salam is a permissible act in itself, due to the hadith: 'The tahrimah is the takbir, and the tahlil is the salam,' narrated by Tirmidhi and others. It is ineffective here because it needs to perform the sajdat al-sahw, so it does not appear without it, and there is no need when considering the lack of return. Thus in al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
[2] His saying: 'by intention of iqamah'; i.e., after the salam before the prostration. As for before the salam, there is no doubt that his obligatory prayer becomes four by consensus, because he has not exited from the sanctity of the prayer by consensus, and similarly after...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage covers three distinct rulings within the chapter of sajdat al-sahw.
First ruling: The effect of salam when sajdat al-sahw is due. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that saying the salam under this condition results in a 'suspended exit' (tawaqquf). The person is considered to have exited the prayer only if he does not subsequently perform the sajdat al-sahw; if he does perform it, it becomes clear that the salam did not cause exit. Muhammad holds that the salam does not remove one from the prayer at all because sajdat al-sahw must be performed within the prayer. The response of the first two imams is that the salam is inherently a permissible act (it can end the prayer), but here its effect is suspended due to the need to perform the prostration; once the prostration is done, the prayer is complete.
Second ruling: Laughing loudly (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates wudu. This is stated briefly.
Third ruling: If one intends iqamah (to make the prayer a resident prayer) after saying the salam but before prostrating for sahw, the obligatory prayer becomes four rak'ahs according to all. If before salam, it is also four by consensus.
The commentary elaborates only the first and third rulings; the second is not expounded.
The hadith evidence for the permissibility of salam is cited: 'Tahrimuha al-takbir wa tahliluha al-taslim' (its prohibition is the takbir and its permissibility is the salam).

Key Terms
موقوفاً (mawqūfan): Suspended, pending the outcome (whether sajdat al-sahw is performed or not).
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud, contagious laughter during prayer.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqāmah): Intention to perform the prayer as a resident (full prayer) rather than a traveller's shortened prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what happens if a person says salam while sajdat al-sahw is due and then prostrates?
A) He has exited the prayer at the salam; his prostration is invalid.
B) He is still in the prayer; the prostration completes it.
C) He is out of the prayer and must repeat it.
D) The prostration is not required because he already exited.

Key Takeaway
When sajdat al-sahw is due, the salam results in a suspended exit: if you later prostrate, you were never out; if you don't, you exited from the moment of salam.

The Suspended Salam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sajdat al-Sahw
Explains the ruling of salam for one who owes sajdat al-sahw and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam from one who owes sajdat al-sahw and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The salam of one who owes sajdat al-sahw is suspended until the prostration is performed or abandoned.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah delves into the ruling of salam for a person who still owes sajdat al-sahw. It reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether such a salam definitively ends the prayer or is suspended until the prostration is done. Understanding this dispute clarifies a key principle: the interaction between obligatory compensations and the exit from prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salam given by a person who still owes sajdat al-sahw. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this salam is 'muwaqqaf' (suspended).
Not a definitive exit nor a stay.
2
State the position of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
The salam removes the person from prayer in a suspended manner: he is not judged to have exited until it is seen whether he prostrates or not.
If he prostrates, it becomes clear he never exited; if he abandons, he exited from the time of salam.
3
Identify the opposing view (Imam Muhammad)
Muhammad holds that the salam does not remove the person from prayer at all, because sajdat al-sahw is wajib to compensate deficiency and must be performed within the prayer's sanctity.
Thus, according to Muhammad, the person remains in prayer until he prostrates, and the salam has no effect on exiting.
4
Follow the dalil for each side
Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf cite the hadith 'tahlil al-salat al-taslim' to show salam is inherently a permitted exit, but here its effect is delayed due to the need to perform sajdat al-sahw. Muhammad relies on the obligation to compensate deficiency within the prayer.
The hadith is general; the need for sajdat al-sahw creates a specific context.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a follower joins an imam who gave salam while owing sajdat al-sahw, then the imam prostrates: according to Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, the follower's prayer is valid; according to Muhammad, it is invalid because the imam never exited.
The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلام من عليه السهو يخرجُهُ عنها موقوفاً حتّى يصح الاقتداء به ، يبطل وضوؤه بالقهقهة، ويصير فرضُه أربعاً بنية الإقامة [1] (سلام من عليه السهو يخرجُهُ عنها موقوفاً حتّى يصح الاقتداء به ، ويبطل وضوؤه بالقهقهة، ويصيرُ فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة () سجود السهو في آخر صلاته ؛ لبطلان السابق بوقوعه في وسط الصلاة، هو الصحيح، وقيل : لا يعيد. كذا في «الهداية»، و«البناية». 1 ] قوله : سلام من...الخ ؛ يعني إذا سلّم في آخر الصلاة وعليه سجود السهو، يخرجه السلام عن تلك الصلاة خروجاً موقوفاً، ومعناه : أنه يتوقف على ظهور عاقبته، ولا يحكم بخروجه ، فإن سجدَ بعد ذلك للسهو تَبَيَّنَ أنه لم يخرجه ، وإن لم يسجد تبين أنه أخرجه من وقت وجوده. وقيل : معنى التوقف أنه وإن كان يخرجُهُ من كلّ وجه لكن على احتمال أن يعود إلى حرمتها بالسجود، وبعد خروجه منها ، فإن سجد عاد وإلا فلا. وصحح في «البدائع» المعنى الأول بناءً على أنّ التحريمة واحدة، فإذا بطلت لا تعود إلا بإعادة، ولم توجد ، وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف . وقال محمد : هو داخل سجد أو لم يسجد ؛ لأنّ عنده سلام من عليه السهو لا يخرجه عن الصلاة أصلاً ؛ لأنها وجبت جبر النقصان، فلا بد أن يكون في إحرام الصلاة. وجوابه من قبلهما : أنّ السلام محلّل في نفسه ؛ لحديث: «تحليلها التسليم» أخرجه الترمذي وغيره، وإنّما لا يعمل هاهنا لحاجته إلى أداء السجدة، فلا يظهر بدونها، ولا حاجة عند اعتبار عدم العود. كذا في «الهداية»، وشروحها. [٢] قوله : بنية الإقامة ؛ أي بعد السلام قبل السجود، أما إن كان قبل السلام فلا شك أنه يصيرُ فرضُهُ أربعاً اتفاقاً ؛ لأنه لم يخرج من حرمة الصلاة اتفاقاً، وكذا بعد إن سجد بعده وإلا فلا : أي المصلّي الذي عليه سجدة السهو إن سَلَّمَ في آخرِ صلاته قبل أن يسجد للسهو يخرجُهُ عن الصَّلاةِ خروجاً موقوفاً، فينظرُ أنَّه إن سجد للسهو بعد ذلك السَّلام يُحْكَمُ بأنه لم يخرج عن الصَّلاة، وإن لم يَسْجُد، بل رَفَضَ الصَّلاة يحكم بأنه قد كان خرج عنها حتّى إن سلم ، ثُمَّ اقتدى به إنسان ، ثم سجد للسهو يكون الاقتداء صحيحاً، ولو لم يسجد بل رَفَضَ الصَّلاةَ لم الاقتداء. السلام والسجود ; لأنه في حرمة الصلاة اتفاقاً، أمّا عند محمد فظاهر، وأما عندهما فلعود حرمة الصلاة بالسجود.
Salam from one who owes sajdat al-sahw takes him out of it in a suspended manner so that following him is valid, his wudu is invalidated by laughter, and his fard becomes four by intention to reside. [Commentary:] Sajdat al-sahw at the end of his prayer; because the previous one is invalidated because it occurred in the middle of the prayer, this is correct, and it is said: he does not repeat. That is in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah. 1 His statement: 'Salam from...' means if he gives salam at the end of the prayer while he owes sajdat al-sahw, the salam removes him from that prayer in a suspended removal. Its meaning: it is suspended on the emergence of its consequence, and he is not judged as having exited. If he then performs sajdat al-sahw, it becomes clear that it did not remove him, and if he does not prostrate, it becomes clear that it removed him from the time of its occurrence. And it is said: the meaning of suspension is that even though it removes him in every respect, there is a possibility that he returns to its sanctity by prostration, and after exiting from it, if he prostrates he returns, otherwise not. In al-Bada'i' the first meaning is verified based on the fact that the tahrima is one, so if it becomes invalidated it does not return except by re-entering, and that has not occurred. And all this according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: he remains inside whether he prostrates or not, because according to him, salam from one who owes sajdat al-sahw does not remove him from the prayer at all, because it is obligated to compensate the deficiency, so it must be within the sanctity of the prayer. The response from the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that salam is a tahlil in itself according to the hadith 'its tahlil is the taslim' recorded by Tirmidhi and others, but it does not operate here due to the need to perform the prostration, so it does not become apparent without it, and there is no need when considering the non-return. That is in al-Hidayah and its commentaries. [2] His statement: 'by intention to reside' i.e. after salam before prostration. As for before salam, there is no doubt that his fard becomes four by agreement, because he has not left the sanctity of the prayer by agreement, and similarly after. 'If he prostrates after it, otherwise not': i.e. the worshipper who owes sajdat al-sahw if he gives salam at the end of his prayer before prostrating for sajdat al-sahw, his salam removes him from the prayer in a suspended removal. It is considered that if he prostrates for sajdat al-sahw after that salam, it is judged that he did not exit the prayer, and if he does not prostrate, but rather abandons the prayer, it is judged that he had exited from it. So if he gives salam, then a person followed him, then he prostrates for sajdat al-sahw, the following is valid. And if he does not prostrate but abandons the prayer, the following is not valid. 'The salam and the prostration; because he is in the sanctity of the prayer by agreement. As for according to Muhammad, it is apparent, and as for according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), because the sanctity of prayer returns by prostration.'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah comments on the ruling of salam for one who owes sajdat al-sahw. The matn states that such a salam is 'suspended' (muwaqqaf). The commentary explains two interpretations of the suspension: (1) it is suspended on the outcome - if he prostrates, it is as if he never exited; if he doesn't, he exited from the time of salam. (2) it removes him completely but with possibility of return. Al-Bada'i' prefers the first because the tahrima is one and cannot be restored without a new one. The commentary then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the suspension view. Muhammad holds that the salam does not remove him at all because sajdat al-sahw is obligatory to compensate the deficiency and must be within the prayer's sanctity. The response from the two shaykhs is that salam is inherently tahlil (permitted exit) based on the hadith 'the tahlil of the prayer is the taslim', but here it is delayed due to the need to perform the prostration. The commentary then clarifies the effect of intention to reside: if the intention is made after salam before prostration, the fard becomes four according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the salam is not final. The final paragraph explains that if he prostrates after salam, the sanctity returns, making following valid. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on istihsan and the hadith for tahlil.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed at the end of prayer to compensate for omissions or errors.
تحليلها التسليم (tahliluha al-taslim): Its permitted exit is the salam; a hadith used to show that salam is the acceptable exit from prayer.
خروج موقوف (khuruj muwaqqaf): Suspended exit from prayer pending prostration; not a definitive exit until the prostration is performed or abandoned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the effect of salam by a person who owes sajdat al-sahw?
A) It definitively ends the prayer.
B) It is suspended; if he later prostrates, he is considered not to have exited.
C) It does not end the prayer at all.
D) It ends the prayer but he must repeat the whole prayer.

Key Takeaway
The salam of one who owes sajdat al-sahw is suspended until the prostration is performed or abandoned, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Correcting the Error: Laughter and Intention Do Not Affect the Suspended Salah
Critical refinement of a matn error

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling on the effects of laughter and intention to reside for a person who has given salam while owing sajdat al-sahw, and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
The suspended state after salam protects wudu and fard from changes that would occur within the prayer.

The commentators of al-Wiqayah identified a famous error in the matn regarding the effect of laughter and intention to reside on a person who has given salam while owing sajdat al-sahw. This lesson clarifies the correct ruling and the reasoning behind it, as established by later Hanafi authorities like al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the specific situation: a person has given salam while still owing a wajib (sajdat al-sahw). The prayer is in a suspended state (mawquf).
2
Recognize the erroneous statements
The original matn claimed that in this state, laughter invalidates wudu and intention to reside changes the fard to four rak\'ahs. These are errors.
3
Present the correction
From al-Durr al-Mukhtar: the correct ruling is that laughter does not invalidate wudu, and intention to reside does not change the fard, whether sajdat al-sahw is performed or not.
4
Understand the rationale
Because sajdat al-sahw is dropped when laughter occurs after effective exit from the prayer, the conditions for those rulings are absent. The prayer is considered ended.
5
Apply the ruling to avoid common mistakes
Use this correction when issuing fatwas or teaching; do not apply the general rule of laughter invalidating wudu to the suspended state.

And more than one have pointed out that it is an error. And it is surprising that the commentator did not realize that what is in the matn is an error. Hence al-Quhistani said in Jami' al-Rumuz: 'Here in al-Wiqayah is a famous oversight. There is no blame on a person for an oversight, but for a mistake. So there is no blame on one who says that what is in al-Wiqayah contradicts what is in its commentary on al-Hidayah, because the commentator is his brother Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah.' End. And he followed the one who erred in this place: al-Ghazzi in Tanwir al-Absar, where he said: 'Salam from one who owes sajdat al-sahw removes him in a suspended manner, so following him is valid, and his wudu is invalidated by laughter, and his fard becomes four by intention to reside if he prostrates, otherwise not.' End. The commentator in al-Durr al-Mukhtar said: 'Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it is an error in the last two. The correct is that his wudu is not invalidated by laughter, nor does his fard change whether he prostrates or not, because the sajdat al-sahw is dropped by laughter, and similarly by the intention, so that it does not occur during the prayer. That is because if a traveler intends to reside after salam, he does not prostrate for sajdat al-sahw, because sajdat al-sahw during the prayer is not prescribed, so his fard does not become four by intention to reside according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and similarly not...'
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement correcting a common error in the matn of al-Wiqayah. The matn had stated that for a person who owes sajdat al-sahw, if he gives salam (which is suspended), his wudu is invalidated by laughter (qahqaha) and his fard becomes four rak'ahs if he intends to reside (niyyat al-iqamah). The commentators point out that this is an error (sahw mashhur). Al-Quhistani notes that the error is famous, and it's surprising that the original commentator (Sadr al-Shari'ah) did not notice it. The correct ruling, as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar, is that laughter does not invalidate his wudu, and his fard does not change to four, whether he prostrates or not. The reason is that the sajdat al-sahw itself falls away due to the laughter (because it occurs after the salam, which is outside the prayer), so the conditions for change are absent. Similarly, the intention to reside after salam does not affect because the prostration is not prescribed during the prayer. Thus the earlier matn is corrected: the rulings on laughter and intention only apply to a person who is still in the prayer (without the suspended status). This refinement shows the importance of verifying matn statements against the authoritative sources.

Key Terms
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter that involves sound and movement; in Hanafi fiqh, it invalidates wudu and salah if it occurs during prayer.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqamah): Intention of a traveler to reside in a place for fifteen days or more, which changes the ruling from qasr to complete prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected ruling, what is the effect of laughter (qahqaha) on the wudu of a person who has given salam while owing sajdat al-sahw?
A) It invalidates his wudu.
B) It does not invalidate his wudu.
C) It invalidates his prayer.
D) It requires a new wudu.

Key Takeaway
Laughter and intention to reside do not invalidate wudu or change fard for a person who has given salam while owing sajdat al-sahw.

The Suspended Exit: Salam Before Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of salam before sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on salam before sujud al-sahw and apply the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf to determine the validity of following, the effect of loud laughter, and the change of obligation by intention of residence.

Core Idea
Salam before sujud al-sahw: exit is suspended until sujud is performed or abandoned.

When a person says salam but still owes sujud al-sahw, the ruling is not straightforward. Imam Muhammad holds that the salam does not exit the prayer, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf view it as a suspended exit. This difference has real consequences for the imam's followability, the effect of loud laughter, and a traveler's intention of residence. In this lesson, we will dissect this intra-Hanafi dispute and learn the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core disagreement
Determine whether salam before sujud al-sahw definitively ends the prayer, or not, or conditionally. This is the pivot of the ikhtilaf.
The three logical possibilities: definitive exit, no exit, suspended exit.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position
According to Muhammad, salam does not exit the prayer at all. The person remains in hurmat al-salah because the wajib sujud must be performed within the prayer.
3
State the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
According to them, salam results in a suspended exit (khuruj mawquf). The final ruling depends on whether sujud follows: if he prostrates, he was never out; if he abandons, the exit is confirmed.
4
Apply to three practical branches
Examine the consequences for iqtida (following), the effect of loud laughter (qahqaha) on wudu, and the change of obligation by intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) under each view.
These branches are the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and correct common error
The relied-upon ruling is that of the two. Note the well-known error in al-Wiqaya and later works that attributed conditional rulings on qahqaha and niyyat to the two. The correct position is unconditional.
Refer to the sharh chain for the correction.

Book of Prayer / Sujud al-Sahw: If he prostrates after it, otherwise no. (Meaning: The person who owes the prostration of forgetfulness, if he says Salam at the end of his prayer before prostrating for forgetfulness, he exits the prayer with a suspended exit. So it is considered: if he prostrates for forgetfulness after that Salam, it is ruled that he did not exit the prayer; if he does not prostrate but rather abandons the prayer, it is ruled that he had exited it. So if he says Salam, then a person follows him, then he prostrates for forgetfulness, the following is valid; if he does not prostrate but abandons the prayer, the following is not valid. And the salam and prostration are because he is in the sacredness of prayer by agreement. As for according to Muhammad, it is apparent; and as for according to the two, because the sacredness of prayer returns by prostration. [1] His saying: 'If he prostrates after it... etc.' Thus mentioned by al-Itqani in Ghayat al-Bayan, and the author of al-Durar, and the author of Multaqa al-Abhar. And more than one have pointed out that it is a mistake. And it is surprising that the commentator did not notice that what is in the text is a mistake. Hence al-Quhistani said in Jami' al-Rumuz: 'In al-Wiqaya here there is a famous oversight. There is no fault in a person for oversight, but for error. So there is no fault for the one who says that what is in al-Wiqaya contradicts what is in its commentary on al-Hidayah, for the commentator is his brother Umar bin Sadr al-Shari'ah.' End. And following him in this error was al-Ghazzi in Tanwir al-Absar where he said: 'The Salam of the one who owes forgetfulness exits him in a suspended manner, so following him is valid, and his ablution is invalidated by loud laughter, and his obligation becomes four by intention of residence if he prostrates, otherwise no.' End. His commentator in al-Durr al-Mukhtar said: 'Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it is an error in the last two. The correct is that his ablution is not invalidated by loud laughter, nor does his obligation change whether he prostrates or not, because the prostration is dropped by loud laughter, and likewise by intention, so that it does not occur during the prayer.' (Footnote 5) That is because if a traveler intends residence after Salam, he does not prostrate for forgetfulness, because the prostration for forgetfulness during prayer was not prescribed, so his obligation does not become four by intention of residence according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and likewise his ablution is not invalidated by loud laughter according to them because it did not encounter the sacredness of prayer, since loud laughter cuts the tahrimah because it is speech, so his exit from prayer is realized, so how can he prostrate for forgetfulness? [1] His saying: 'And if he says Salam... etc.' He said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: According to him, i.e., according to Muhammad, the Salam of one who owes forgetfulness does not exit him from prayer at all, because it (the prostration) was obligated to compensate for the deficiency, and it must be in the state of prayer. And according to the two, it exits him on a suspended basis. And the difference appears in the validity of following, and in the nullification of purity by loud laughter, and the change of obligation by intention of residence in this situation. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. And its apparent meaning is that purity is nullified according to him by loud laughter absolutely, and according to the two: if he returns to prostration, it is nullified, otherwise not, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is an error, for there is no detail regarding prostration or not according to them, because loud laughter caused the dropping of Sujud al-Sahw according to all, due to the loss of the sacredness of prayer because it is speech. The ruling is nullification according to him, and no nullification according to them, as stated in al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi. And its apparent meaning also is that if he intends residence, the matter is suspended according to the two: if he prostrates, completion is necessary for him, otherwise no; and according to Muhammad, he completes absolutely. And he stated in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it is also an error. For the ruling in it is that if he intends residence before prostration, his obligation does not change according to the two, and Sujud al-Sahw is dropped from him, because if he prostrates, he has returned to the sacredness of prayer, so his obligation changes to four, so his prostration occurs during the prayer, so it is not considered and there is no benefit in engaging in it. And according to him, he completes it as four.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling of a person who says Salam before performing Sujud al-Sahw (the prostration of forgetfulness). The core issue is whether the Salam definitively ends the prayer or not. According to Imam Muhammad, the Salam does not exit the prayer at all; the person remains in the sacred state of prayer (hurmat al-salah) because the prostration is obligatory to compensate for a deficiency and must occur within the prayer. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the Salam results in a suspended exit (khuruj mawquf): if the person later performs the prostration, it retroactively indicates that he never left the prayer; if he abandons the prostration, it becomes clear that he had exited at the moment of Salam. This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in three areas: the validity of following (iqtida') this imam, the effect of loud laughter (qahqaha) on ablution, and the change of the obligatory rak'at count by intention of residence (niyyat al-iqama) for a traveler. The text also corrects a widespread mistake in al-Wiqaya and later works that attributed to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) a conditional ruling on qahqaha and niyyat al-iqama. The correct position according to the two is that loud laughter always drops the sujud and does not invalidate ablution because the salam has already caused a suspended exit; similarly, intention of residence after salam does not change the obligation because it would place the sujud after the prayer. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that the person is still in prayer, so loud laughter would invalidate ablution, and intention of residence would necessitate completing four rak'at. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), as affirmed by later authorities.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer; must be performed while still in the state of prayer.
خروج موقوف (khuruj mawquf): A suspended exit from prayer where the status is contingent upon subsequent action (sujud or abandonment).
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter in prayer; considered speech that invalidates the prayer's sacredness (hurma).
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): For a traveler, intending to reside in a place for at least 15 days, which changes the travel ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The salam becomes a definitive exit and the prayer is considered ended.
C) The person must still perform sujud later even if outside prayer.
D) The prayer is nullified and the person must restart.

Key Takeaway
Salam before sujud al-sahw results in a suspended exit; the mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that the ruling depends on subsequent prostration.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Laughter After Salām and Intention to Continue Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qahqaha after salām and niyyat iqāmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn regarding qahqaha after salām and derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for wudū and fard prayer.

Core Idea
Laughter after salām nullifies wudū only if the prayer hasn't exited—dispute hinges on when salām ends prayer.

The final salām is normally the exit from prayer, but when sajd al-sahw is owed, a dispute arises: does the prayer remain sacred until the prostration is performed? Imam Muhammad holds it does; the Sahibayn hold it exits conditionally. This directly affects the rulings on laughter after salām and the intention to continue. Let us examine the reasoning and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base case and ruling
The matn states: if one says salām, then laughs, then prostrates, wudū is nullified. If he does not prostrate, no nullification. Also, if he says salām then intends iqāmah, then prostrates, the fard becomes four.
Note the conditionality tied to prostration.
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's view
For Imam Muhammad, salām of a forgetful person does not exit the prayer at all because sajd al-sahw must be performed within the prayer's sanctity. Hence laughter after salām occurs in the prayer, nullifying wudū regardless of prostration.
Thus his position is absolute nullification upon laughter, and absolute change to four upon niyyat iqāmah.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's view
For the Sahibayn, salām exits the prayer conditionally (mu'allaq). The prayer is considered exited unless one returns to prostration. Hence laughter after salām is after prayer—it does not nullify wudū. The intention to continue only changes fard if one actually returns to prostration.
This is a nuanced conditional exit.
4
Correct a common misunderstanding
Some sources claim that according to the Sahibayn, wudū is nullified if one returns to prostration after laughter. The commentary refutes this as an error: the correct position is that wudū is never nullified by laughter after salām according to them, because the prayer has already been exited (even if conditionally).
The laughter cuts tahrīmah, which is only possible if the prayer is still ongoing.
5
Apply to the practical scenario
If a laughing person prostrates after salām: according to Imam Muhammad, wudū invalid and must renew; according to Sahibayn, wudū valid and prayer can continue. For niyyat iqāmah: according to Imam Muhammad, fard changes to four; according to Sahibayn, only if one actually returns to prostration.
The difference is clear in the need to repeat wudū.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا سلم ، ثُمَّ قهقه ، ثُمَّ سَجَدَ يُحْكَم ببطلان وضوئه، إذ القهقهة وجدت في خلال الصَّلاة، ولو لم يسجد بل رفض لم يبطل وضوؤه. ولو سلم ، ثُمَّ نوى الإقامة، ثُمَّ سَجَدَ للسهو صارَ هذا الفرضُ أربعاً ؛ لأنَّ نية الإقامةِ وُجِدَت بعد الصلاة. [١] قوله : وإذا سلم ... الخ ؛ قال في «البحر الرائق»: عنده ؛ أي عند محمد ه ، سلامُ مَن عليه السهو لا يخرجه من الصلاة أصلاً ؛ لأنها وجبت جبراً للنقصان، ولا بد أن يكون في إحرام الصلاة. وعندهما يخرجه على سبيل التوقف، ويظهر الاختلاف في صحة الاقتداء، وفي انتقاض الطهارة بالقهقهة، وتغيّر الفرض بنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة. كذا في «الهداية» (١) ، وغيرها. وظاهره أنّ الطهارة تنتقض عنده بالقهقهة مطلقاً، وعندهما إن عاد إلى السجود انتقضت وإلا فلا كما صرّح به في غاية «البيان»، وهو غلط ، فإنّه لا تفصيل فيه بين السجودِ وعدمه عندهما ؛ لأنَّ القهقهة أوجبت سقوط سجود السهو عند الكلّ ؛ لفوات حرمة الصَّلاة ؛ لأنها كلام، وإنما الحكم هو النقض عنده، وعدمه عندهما، كما صرّح به في «المحيط» و«شرح الطحاوي». وظاهره أيضاً أنه لو نوى الإقامة فالأمر موقوف عندهما إن سجدَ لزمه الإتمام ، وإلا فلا، وعند محمد الله يتم مطلقاً ، وقد صَرَّحَ به في «غاية البيان»، وهو غلط أيضاً ؛ فإن الحكم فيه إذا نوى الإقامة قبل السجود أنّه لا يتغيَّر فرضه عندهما، ويسقط عنه سجود السهو؛ لأنه لـو سـجد فقد عاد إلى حرمة الصلاة، فيتغير فرضه أربعاً، فيقعُ سجوده في خلال الصلاة فلا يعتد به ولا فائدة في الاشتغال به، وعنده يتمها أربعاً، يبطل وضوؤه بقهقهة عندهما ؛ لأنها لم تصادف حرمة الصلاة إذ القهقهة قاطعة للتحريمة ؛ لأنها كلام فيتحقق خروجه عن الصلاة، فكيف يسجد للسهو، وتمامه في «حاشية الشرنبلالي على الدرر (١: ١٥٤) ، و(الدر المختار (۱): ٥٠٤ ) ، و (مجمع الأنهر (۱ : ١٥٢)، و«رد المحتار» (١ : ٥٠٤).
And if he says salām, then laughs, then prostrates, it is ruled that his wudū is nullified, because the laughter occurred during the prayer. And if he does not prostrate but abandons it, his wudū is not nullified. And if he says salām, then intends to continue (al-iqāmah), then prostrates for forgetfulness, this prayer becomes four (rak'ahs); because the intention of iqāmah occurred after the prayer. [1] His statement: 'And if he says salām... etc.' He said in al-Bahr al-Rā'iq: According to him, i.e., according to Muhammad, the salām of one who has forgetfulness does not remove him from the prayer at all; because it (the prostration) was obligated to compensate for the deficiency, and it must be within the sanctity of the prayer. And according to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad al-Shaybānī), it removes him conditionally. And the difference appears in the validity of following (as imām), in the nullification of purity by laughter, and the change of the obligatory prayer by the intention of iqāmah in this case. Thus in al-Hidāyah and others. And its apparent meaning is that purity is nullified according to him by laughter absolutely, and according to the two, if he returns to prostration it is nullified, otherwise not, as stated in Ghāyat al-Bayān. But this is an error, for there is no distinction between prostrating and not prostrating according to the two; because the laughter necessitated the dropping of the prostration of forgetfulness according to all, due to the loss of the sanctity of the prayer, because it is speech. The ruling is nullification according to him, and not according to the two, as stated in al-Muhīt and Sharh al-Tahāwī. And its apparent meaning also that if he intended iqāmah, the matter is suspended according to the two: if he prostrates, completion becomes necessary, otherwise not; and according to Muhammad, it is completed absolutely. And he stated this in Ghāyat al-Bayān, which is also an error. For the ruling in this case, when he intends iqāmah before prostration, is that his obligatory prayer does not change according to the two, and the prostration of forgetfulness drops from him. Because if he prostrates, he returns to the sanctity of the prayer, so his obligatory prayer changes to four, and his prostration occurs during the prayer, so it is not considered and there is no benefit in engaging in it. And according to him, he completes it as four. His wudū is nullified by laughter according to the two, because it did not coincide with the sanctity of the prayer, as laughter cuts the sanctification (tahrīmah), because it is speech, thus his exit from the prayer is realized. So how can he prostrate for forgetfulness? And its completion is in Hāshiyat al-Shurnublāliyyah 'alā al-Durar (1:154), and al-Durr al-Mukhtār (1:504), and Majma' al-Anhur (1:152), and Radd al-Muhtār (1:504).
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on laughter (qahqaha) after saying the final salām in prayer, and the effect of intending to continue prayer (niyyat al-iqāmah) after salām. The base text (matn) rules: if one says salām, then laughs, then prostrates for forgetfulness, his wudū is nullified because the laughter occurred during the prayer (since according to Imam Muhammad, salām from one who owes sajd al-sahw does not exit the prayer). If he does not prostrate, wudū is not nullified. If he says salām, intends to continue, then prostrates, the prayer becomes four rak'ahs. The commentary explains that according to Imam Muhammad, salām of one who owes sajd al-sahw does not exit the prayer at all, because the prostration is obligatory to compensate for deficiency and must be performed within the prayer's sanctity. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the salām exits the prayer conditionally (on a suspended basis). Based on this, differences arise in following the imam, nullification of wudū by laughter, and change of the fard prayer by intention to continue. The commentary then corrects a misunderstanding: it is claimed that according to the Sahibayn, if one returns to prostration, wudū is nullified, otherwise not. But the correct view is that according to them, wudū is never nullified by laughter after salām, because the laughter occurs after exiting the prayer (since their view is that salām exits, though conditionally). Similarly, for niyyat al-iqāmah, the Sahibayn say the prayer does not change unless one actually prostrates, but Imam Muhammad says it changes absolutely. The commentary clarifies that if one intends iqāmah before prostrating, according to the Sahibayn the fard does not change and sajd al-sahw drops, because if he prostrates he re-enters the prayer and his fard changes to four, but the prostration would be during the prayer—invalid. According to Muhammad, he completes four. The passage concludes by stating that according to the Sahibayn, wudū is not nullified because the laughter did not occur within the sanctity of the prayer, as laughter cuts the tahrīmah. References are given to major Hanafi works.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Laughter with audible sound; in Hanafi fiqh, it invalidates prayer if it occurs during the prayer.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqāmah): The intention to continue the prayer (to remain in the state of prayer) after having said salām.
تحريمة (tahrīmah): The initial takbīr that sanctifies the prayer and creates a sacred state; major speech or laughter breaks this state and invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the effect of laughing after the final salām if the person then prostrates for sajd al-sahw?
A) Wudū nullified, prayer becomes four with niyyat iqāmah.
B) Wudū valid, prayer valid as is.
C) Wudū nullified, prayer invalid.
D) Wudū valid, prayer becomes four.

Key Takeaway
The effect of laughter after salām on wudū hinges on whether the prayer has exited—a dispute between Imam Muhammad (no exit) and Sahibayn (conditional exit), with practical consequences for wudū and fard change.

Salām with Intent to Exit: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tahlīl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salām with intent to cut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of salām when pronounced with intent to cut the prayer, and explain the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A salām pronounced with intent to exit before completing wajib does not exit the prayer according to Imam Muhammad; the Sahibayn consider it a conditional tahlīl.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nature of the final salām when it is pronounced with the deliberate intention of cutting the prayer short after having omitted a wajib (obligatory element). The base text states that such an intention is void, but the commentary reveals two distinct positions from the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage begins with 'He forgets and says salām with the intention of cutting'. Determine what element was forgotten and what the intention is.
The forgotten element is a wajib (obligatory act) such as a sajdah or tashahhud.
2
Understand Imam Muhammad's ruling
Imam Muhammad holds that this salām is not a tahlīl (permitted exit) because the prayer is incomplete. Therefore the intention to cut is void and the tahrīmah remains.
The commentary states: 'this salām is not a tahlīl according to Muhammad'.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's view
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the salām is a tahlīl on a conditional basis. If the person intended it as a permanent tahlīl, that intention is void because it changes the prescribed act, but the salām itself can still be effective conditionally.
The key phrase: 'it is a tahlīl on a conditional basis'.
4
Apply the practical difference
According to Imam Muhammad, the person must return and perform sajd al-sahw. According to the Sahibayn, if he intentionally said salām knowing the obligation, that obligation drops. Later Hanafi fatwa follows the Sahibayn.
This shows the importance of knowing which position is operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سَهَا وسلّم بنية القطع بطل نيته، شكٍّ أوّل مرة أنه كم صلى استأنف، وإن كثر أَخَذَ مَا غَلَبَ على ظَنُّه (سَهَا وسلّم بنية القطع بطل نيته (۳) حتّى تكون تحريمتُه باقيةً كما مرّ. شك أول مرة " أنه كم صلّى استأنف ، وإن كثر (۱) أَخَذَ ما غَلَبَ على ظنّه ) ويسجد في آخر صلاته. كذا في «المحيط»(۲). [١] قوله : سها وسلّم ؛ يعني سها عن واجب، فوجب عليه سجود السهو، وسلم بنية الخروج عن الصلاة فنيته باطلة، وتحريمته باقية، فعليه أن يعود إلى سجودِ السهو؛ لأنّ هذا السلام غير محلّل ع عند محمد الله ، ومتى قصد تحليله فقد قصد تغيّر المشروع، فلغت نيته. (وعندهما: هو محلّل على سبيل التوقف، فمتى قصد أن يجعله محللا على الثبات، فقد قصد تغيير المشروع. كذا في «الكفاية». وذكر في «فتح القدير» و«البدائع» هاهنا صوراً كثيرة، منها : إنه إذا سلّم بنية القطع . ذاكراً إنّ عليه سجدة تلاوة أو قراءة التشهد الأخير سقطت عنه ؛ لأنَّ سلامه عمداً يخرجه عن الصلاة، ولا تفسد صلاته لتمام الأركان، وتكون ناقصة لترك الواجب، وكذا لو سلم وعليه تلاويّة أو سهوية ذاكراً لهما، ولو نسي السهو أو سجدة تلاوة أو صلبيّة يلزمه ذلك ما دام في المسجد. (٢) قوله : بطل نيته ؛ بشرط أن لا يتحوّل عن القبلة، ولا يتكلّم، فإن فعل بطلت تحريمته. كذا في «النهاية». له. [٣] قوله : أول مرة ؛ يعني أوّل سهو وقع له من عين البلوغ، ولم يكن ذلك عادة [٤] قوله : استأنف ؛ أي ترك ما صلّى وابتدأ بالصلاة؛ وذلك لأنه وردت في هذا (۱) بأن عرض له مرتين في عمره على ما عليه أكثرهم، أو في صلاته على ما اختاره فخر الإسلام، وفي المجتبى»: وقيل مرتين في سنة، ولعله على قول السرخسي. ينظر: (رد المحتار).
He forgets and says salām with the intention of cutting (the prayer); his intention is void. He doubts for the first time how many he has prayed; he starts over. And if it occurs frequently, he acts upon his dominant opinion. And he prostrates at the end of his prayer. Thus in al-Muhīt. [1] His statement: 'He forgets and says salām' means he forgot an obligatory (act), so sajd al-sahw became obligatory upon him, and he said salām with the intention of exiting the prayer; his intention is void, and his tahrīmah remains, so he must return to the prostration of forgetfulness. Because this salām is not a tahlīl (permitted exit) according to Muhammad. And when he intended it as tahlīl, he intended to change what is prescribed, so his intention is null. (And according to the two, it is a tahlīl on a conditional basis. So when he intended to make it a permanent tahlīl, he intended to change what is prescribed. Thus in al-Kifāyah.) And in Fath al-Qadīr and al-Badā'i', many cases are mentioned here, including: If he says salām with the intention of cutting, knowing that he owes a sajdat al-tilāwah or reciting the final tashahhud, they drop from him; because his intentional salām takes him out of the prayer, and his prayer does not become corrupt due to the completion of the pillars, but it becomes deficient due to leaving an obligatory act. Similarly, if he says salām while he owes a tilāwah-prostration or forgetfulness-prostration, knowing them. And if he forgets the forgetfulness-prostration or a tilāwah-prostration or a prayer-prostration, it is required of him as long as he is in the mosque. (2) His statement: 'His intention is void' is conditional on his not turning away from the qiblah and not speaking; if he does so, his tahrīmah is nullified. Thus in al-Nihāyah. For him. [3] His statement: 'First time' means the first forgetfulness that occurs to him since reaching puberty, and it was not habitual. [4] His statement: 'He starts over' means he leaves what he prayed and begins the prayer anew. That is because there is a tradition in this regard... (1) That it occurs to him twice in his lifetime according to most, or in his prayer according to Fakhr al-Islām, and in al-Mujtabā: 'twice in a year' is also said, and perhaps it is according to al-Sarakhsī. Refer to Radd al-Muhtār.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct issues within sajd al-sahw: (1) the ruling on one who forgets an obligatory element and then says the final salām with the intention of exiting the prayer, and (2) the ruling on one who doubts the number of rak'ahs performed. The base matn states that if one forgets (i.e., omits a wajib) and says salām with the intention of cutting the prayer, his intention is void, meaning the prayer is not exited. If he doubts for the first time how many rak'ahs he has prayed, he must restart the prayer. If doubt occurs frequently, he acts upon his predominant guess and prostrates at the end. The commentary explains the first issue: if one forgets a wajib, sajd al-sahw becomes obligatory. He then says salām intending to exit. According to Imam Muhammad, this salām is not a valid tahlīl (permitted exit) — it does not exit the prayer, so his intention is void and his tahrīmah (sanctity) remains. He must return and perform sajd al-sahw. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the salām is a tahlīl on a conditional basis. The commentary from Fath al-Qadīr and al-Badā'i' adds scenarios: if one intentionally says salām knowing he owes a sajdat al-tilāwah or the final tashahhud, those obligations drop; the prayer is valid (since pillars are complete) but deficient (for leaving wajib). If he forgets about the sajdah obligations, they remain required as long as he is in the mosque. A condition for the voidness of the intention is that he does not turn from qiblah or speak; otherwise the tahrīmah is truly lost. On the second issue: 'first time' refers to the first occurrence of such doubt since puberty, provided it is not habitual. If it is the first time, he must restart because there is no predominant opinion to rely on. If frequent (defined as twice or more per prayer or per lifetime, with varying opinions), he acts on his dominant assumption and does sajd al-sahw. The commentary cites definitions from scholars like Fakhr al-Islām and al-Sarakhsī.

Key Terms
نية القطع (niyyat al-qat'): The intention to cut short or exit the prayer entirely by saying the final salām.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The sanctity of the prayer that prevents invalidating acts; it is established by the opening takbīr and remains until the closing salām.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the ruling on salām with intent to cut after forgetting a wajib?
A) The salām is invalid and prayer continues.
B) The salām is a conditional tahlīl meaning obligations may drop.
C) The prayer is void.
D) The person must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether salām with intent to cut after missing a wajib is a valid exit; the relied-upon view considers it a conditional exit, meaning obligations may drop.

Doubting Rak'ahs: First-Time vs Frequent Doubt in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on doubt of rak'ahs (first-time vs frequent)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between first-time doubt and frequent doubt in prayer, and apply the Hanafi ruling for each case.

Core Idea
First-time doubt requires restarting the prayer; frequent doubt allows acting on the predominant opinion with sajd al-sahw.

The second part of the passage addresses a common challenge in prayer: uncertainty about the number of rak'ahs performed. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on whether the doubt is an isolated incident or a recurring occurrence. This distinction ensures that the worshipper does not fall into unnecessary difficulty while maintaining the integrity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first-time doubt scenario
The matn says: 'If he doubts for the first time how many he has prayed, he restarts.' Understand that this is the first occurrence of such doubt in his life since puberty, and it is not habitual.
The commentary specifies the conditions for this ruling.
2
Identify the frequent doubt scenario
The matn says: 'If it occurs frequently, he acts upon his dominant opinion and prostrates at the end.' Determine what 'frequent' means based on scholarly definitions.
The commentary gives various opinions: twice in a lifetime, twice in a prayer, or twice in a year.
3
Apply the ruling to a practical case
Given a scenario, decide whether the doubt is first-time or frequent, and state the required action: restart, or continue based on predominant opinion and perform sajd al-sahw.
The key is to determine the frequency and whether there is a clear dominant opinion.

And if he forgets the forgetfulness-prostration or a tilāwah-prostration or a prayer-prostration, it is required of him as long as he is in the mosque. (2) His statement: 'His intention is void' is conditional on his not turning away from the qiblah and not speaking; if he does so, his tahrīmah is nullified. Thus in al-Nihāyah. For him. [3] His statement: 'First time' means the first forgetfulness that occurs to him since reaching puberty, and it was not habitual. [4] His statement: 'He starts over' means he leaves what he prayed and begins the prayer anew. That is because there is a tradition in this regard... (1) That it occurs to him twice in his lifetime according to most, or in his prayer according to Fakhr al-Islām, and in al-Mujtabā: 'twice in a year' is also said, and perhaps it is according to al-Sarakhsī. Refer to Radd al-Muhtār.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct issues within sajd al-sahw: (1) the ruling on one who forgets an obligatory element and then says the final salām with the intention of exiting the prayer, and (2) the ruling on one who doubts the number of rak'ahs performed. The base matn states that if one forgets (i.e., omits a wajib) and says salām with the intention of cutting the prayer, his intention is void, meaning the prayer is not exited. If he doubts for the first time how many rak'ahs he has prayed, he must restart the prayer. If doubt occurs frequently, he acts upon his predominant guess and prostrates at the end. The commentary explains the first issue: if one forgets a wajib, sajd al-sahw becomes obligatory. He then says salām intending to exit. According to Imam Muhammad, this salām is not a valid tahlīl (permitted exit) — it does not exit the prayer, so his intention is void and his tahrīmah (sanctity) remains. He must return and perform sajd al-sahw. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the salām is a tahlīl on a conditional basis. The commentary from Fath al-Qadīr and al-Badā'i' adds scenarios: if one intentionally says salām knowing he owes a sajdat al-tilāwah or the final tashahhud, those obligations drop; the prayer is valid (since pillars are complete) but deficient (for leaving wajib). If he forgets about the sajdah obligations, they remain required as long as he is in the mosque. A condition for the voidness of the intention is that he does not turn from qiblah or speak; otherwise the tahrīmah is truly lost. On the second issue: 'first time' refers to the first occurrence of such doubt since puberty, provided it is not habitual. If it is the first time, he must restart because there is no predominant opinion to rely on. If frequent (defined as twice or more per prayer or per lifetime, with varying opinions), he acts on his dominant assumption and does sajd al-sahw. The commentary cites definitions from scholars like Fakhr al-Islām and al-Sarakhsī.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt about the number of rak'ahs performed during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a person who doubts the number of rak'ahs for the first time?
A) He continues based on predominant opinion.
B) He restarts the prayer.
C) He chooses the smaller number.
D) He completes and repeats later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between first-time doubt (requires restart) and frequent doubt (act on predominant opinion with sajd al-sahw) to balance certainty and practicality.
