(1)
[١] قوله : وهو المقصود ؛ أي السجود، وهو المقصود من القيام ؛ لكونه غاية التعظيم، هكذا في «الهداية ) ، وغيره ، وفيه بحث مذكور في «فتح القدير».
[٢] قوله : ومومئ ؛ يعني من شرع صلاته بالإيماء، لتعذر غيره ، فصح في أثناء صلاته، وزال مرضُهُ فقَدِرَ على الركوع والسجودِ بطلت صلاته، ويجب عليه أن يبتدأ بها راكعاً وساجداً، ولا يبني على ما مضى ؛ لأنه لا يجوز اقتداء الراكع بالمومئ ، فكذا البناء ؛ لئلا يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف، وهذا على قول أئمتنا الثلاثة، وفيه خلاف زفره .
وأمَّا مَن صَلَّى قاعداً يركع ويسجد لعذر فقدر في أثناء صلاته على القيام يجوز له البناء عندهما، خلافاً لمحمد له ، وهذا الخلاف مبني على جواز اقتداء القائم بالقاعد، فعندهما يجوز، وهو الأصح لما ثبت في السنن: «أنَّ النَّبي صلّى في مرض موته قاعداً، والنَّاسُ خلفه قيام (۳) ، فكذا يجوز البناء ، وعنده لا يجوز، فكذا البناء.
(۱) «الهداية» (٢ : ٦).
(۲) فتح القدير (٢) : (٦) ، والبحث هو : وقد يمنع أن شرعيته لهذا على وجه الحصر بل له ولما في نفسه من التعظيم كما يشاهد في الشاهد من اعتباره كذلك حتى يحبه أهل التجبر لذلك، فإذا فات أحد التعظيمين صار مطلوباً بما فيه نفسه. ويدل على نفي هذه الدعوى أن من قدر على القعود والركوع والسجود لا القيام وجب القعود مع أنه ليس في السجود عقيبه تلك النهاية لعدم مسبوقيته بالقيام.
(۳) فعن عائشة رضي الله عنها: «كان أبو بكر يصلي ، وهو قائم بصلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والناس يصلون بصلاة أبي بكر والنبي قاعد في (صحيح البخاري (١) : (٢٤٣)، و(صحیح مسلم (۱ :
۳۰۱) ، و (صحيح ابن خزيمة» (١) : ١٢٦)، وغيرهم.
Book of Prayer: Prayer of the Sick. And one who gestures [i.e., prays with gestures] and then becomes healthy during the prayer must restart. And one who prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, and then becomes healthy [able to stand] during the prayer may build [upon what he has already prayed] while standing. [1] Because sitting is closer to prostration, and prostration is the intended purpose because it is the ultimate form of humility. And 'one who gestures and becomes healthy during the prayer must restart' means he begins anew. 'And one who sits, bowing and prostrating, and then becomes healthy may build upon his prayer while standing.' 285 Legally, it is an act of worship without standing, as in the prostration of recitation. And standing alone is not prescribed as worship. If one prostrates to other than Allah, he disbelieves, but not so for standing. When one is unable to perform the original [obligation], the means falls away, like ablution for prayer and going out for Friday prayer. [1] His saying: 'And it is the intended purpose' i.e., prostration is the intended purpose from standing because it is the ultimate form of humility. This is in al-Hidayah and others, and there is a discussion mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. [2] His saying: 'And one who gestures' means one who began his prayer with gestures due to inability to do otherwise, then during his prayer he recovers and becomes able to bow and prostrate – his prayer is invalidated, and he must begin it anew bowing and prostrating. He does not build upon what has passed because it is not permissible for one bowing to follow one gesturing. Similarly, building upon it [is not allowed] lest a strong [prayer] be built upon a weak one. This is the saying of our three imams, and there is a difference of opinion from Zufar. As for one who prays sitting, bowing and prostrating due to an excuse, then during his prayer he becomes able to stand – he is permitted to build upon it according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], contrary to Muhammad [in another view]. This difference is based on the permissibility of a standing person following a sitting person. According to the two, it is permissible, and this is the most correct, as established in the Sunan: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed sitting during his terminal illness while the people behind him were standing.' Thus, building upon it is permissible. According to him [Muhammad], it is not permissible, and so building is not permissible. (1) al-Hidayah 2:6. (2) Fath al-Qadir 2:6, and the discussion is: It may be denied that its prescription is exclusively for this, rather it is for this and for what is in itself of humility, as observed in practice, such that the arrogant dislike it. So when one of the two [acts of] humility is lost, it is required for what it contains. Evidence for negating this claim is that one who is able to sit, bow, and prostrate but not stand must sit even though there is not after it [i.e., after sitting] that ultimate end due to lack of being preceded by standing. (3) From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Abu Bakr was praying standing, leading the prayer of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the people were praying led by Abu Bakr, while the Prophet was sitting' (Sahih al-Bukhari 1:243, Sahih Muslim 1:301, Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah 1:126, and others).
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on two rulings from the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding change in capacity during prayer. The first ruling: someone who begins prayer with gestures due to inability, then recovers the ability to bow and prostrate during the prayer – his prayer becomes invalid, and he must restart from the beginning. The reason given is that bowing/prostrating is the essential act of worship, and gestures are a substitute. When the excuse ceases, the substitute falls away, analogous to how one who cannot perform wudu does tayammum, but when water is found, wudu becomes obligatory. The second ruling: someone who prays sitting with actual bowing and prostrating, then recovers the ability to stand – according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, he may continue from where he left off while standing. This is based on the permissibility of a standing person following a sitting imam, as established by the hadith of the Prophet's illness where he sat and the companions stood behind him. Imam Muhammad reportedly differed in one narration, holding that building is not allowed because the stronger action cannot be built on the weaker, similar to the first case. However, the text declares the view of the two as 'al-asah' (most correct). The discussion also notes that Imam Zufar disagreed with the first ruling, opining that the prayer remains valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the consensus of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) for the first, and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad for the second.

Key Terms
قاعد (qā'id): One who prays sitting with actual bowing and prostration (not gestures).
اقتداء القائم بالقاعد (iqtidā' al-qā'im bi-al-qā'id): The act of a standing person following a sitting imam in prayer. Hanafi validates this based on hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what is the ruling for a person who prays sitting with bowing and prostration due to an excuse and then recovers the ability to stand during the prayer?
A) He must restart the prayer from the beginning.
B) He may continue from where he left off while standing.
C) He must continue sitting for the remainder.
D) His prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Recovering standing during prayer allows building because the hadith validates standing-to-sitting connection, and standing is not a pillar but a condition.
